Any partnership, company, corporation, trust or other entity in which an individual applicant is a member, shareholder, director or officer, or in which such entity acts as a surrogate for such applicant, shall also be subject to the prohibition contained in this section. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(O), 32-205(6)(K); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(O), 32-205(6)(K)) 
Sec. 6-57. - Corporate and partnership applicants. 
(a)  If the applicant is a partnership or limited liability company, all members of the partnership must be qualified to obtain a license and must make sworn statements of these qualifications. 
(b)  If the applicant is a corporation, the manager of the proposed licensed premises must be qualified to obtain a license and must make a sworn statement of these qualifications. A corporate license applicant shall appoint and designate to the board of commissioners an agent authorized to receive service of process under the laws of the state. If no such designation is made, the board may serve or notify the applicant or license holder at any address of the applicant or license holder known to the board. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(I), (J), 32-205(6)(N), (O); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(I), (J), 32-205(6)(N)) 
Sec. 6-58. - Adequate participation. 
A license may be denied to any applicant where it appears that the applicant would not have adequate financial participation in the proposed business to direct and manage its affairs, or where it appears that the applicant is intended to be a mere surrogate for a person who would not otherwise qualify for a license for any reason whatsoever. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(K), 32-205(6)(F); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(K), 32-205(6)(F)) 
Secs. 6-59—6-89. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - LICENSE APPLICATION 

Sec. 6-90. - Guidelines. 
Application for a license shall be made on forms furnished by the board of commissioners according to the following guidelines: 
(1)  All license applications shall be presented in person to the clerk. 
(2)  In addition to the completion and submission of an application form as required by the board, each applicant shall attach thereto a completed form with all attachments and requirements for a state license. 
(3)  Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-3-2, the applicant shall furnish a complete set of fingerprints to be forwarded to the state bureau of investigation, which shall search the files of the state crime information center for any instance of criminal activity during the two years immediately preceding the date of the application. The state bureau of investigation shall also submit the fingerprints to the Federal Bureau of Investigation under the rules established by the United States Department of Justice for processing and identification of records. The federal record, if any, shall be obtained and returned to the board. 
(4)  All licenses shall be valid only for the calendar year indicated thereon and no such license may be renewed. A licensee who desires to continue in business during the next calendar year must make a new application for such year to the clerk prior to November 15 of the present year. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(5); 32-205(4); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(5), 32-205(4)) 
Secs. 6-91—6-108. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - PREMISES 

Sec. 6-109. - Separate license. 
(a)  A separate license shall be required for each place of business, as defined herein. 
(b)  In addition, each pouring license granted will enable the licensee to sell the malt beverages and wine for consumption only in the areas of the premises allowed by state statutory laws and regulations. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(D), 32-205(8); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(D), 32-205(8)) 
Sec. 6-110. - Diagram of building. 
(a)  No license shall be issued to any person making a first-time application for a particular location unless complete and detailed diagrams of the building in which the business will be located and the outside premises are attached to the application, or unless proposed plans and specifications and a building permit of a proposed building to be built are attached to the application. If a person is making application for a renewal license for a location for which a license was granted for the previous year, such person shall sign an affidavit, under oath, in lieu of submitting the aforesaid plans and specifications, that there has been no change in the plans of said building. The completed building or the proposed building shall comply with all ordinances of the board of commissioners, rules and regulations of the state revenue commissioner, and the statutory laws of the state. Upon completion, the proposed building shall be subject to final inspection and approval by the building inspector. 
(b)  Each applicant for a license shall attach to his or her application evidence of ownership of the building or proposed building, or a copy of the lease if the applicant is leasing the building. 
(c)  Licensees shall provide on the premises for which the license is issued adequate sanitary toilet facilities as required by the health and building codes, and the building shall be adequately illuminated so that all hallways, passageways and open areas may be clearly seen by customers therein. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(E), 32-205(9); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(E), 32-205(9)) 
Sec. 6-111. - Distance requirements. 
No license shall be granted to any person unless the entire business premises of the proposed location is situated beyond 100 yards from the property line of any church and not less than 200 yards from any schoolyard or college campus, and not less than 100 yards from any building used as an alcohol rehabilitation center. The distance shall be measured by the most direct route of travel on the ground. Each first-time application for a package or pouring malt beverage and wine license shall include a scale drawing of the location of the proposed premises showing the distance to the nearest church, school, and alcohol rehabilitation center and a certificate of a registered surveyor that such location complies with this section. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(C), 32-205(10); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(C), 32-205(10)) 
Sec. 6-112. - Inspections. 
The business premises of the licensee shall be made available for inspection at any and all times by officers or officials authorized to conduct such inspections. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(15), 32-205(20); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(15), 32-205(20)) 
Sec. 6-113. - Days of operation. 
No licensee shall furnish, sell or offer for sale any malt beverages and/or wine under this chapter at any of the following times: 
(1)  At any time on Christmas Day; or 
(2)  At any time in violation of a state statutory law, state rules or regulations, local ordinance or regulations. 
Licensees holding a license for sale of malt beverages and wine for consumption off premises ("package sales") may sell such beverages on Sundays in compliance with all other applicable state laws. However, sales for consumption on premises ("pouring sales") and sales by alcoholic beverage caterers are prohibited on Sundays. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(7)(b)(ii—iv), 32-205(11); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(7)(b)(ii—iv), 32-205(11); Ord. No. 2012-003, § 1(exh. A), 10-2-2012) 
Sec. 6-114. - Gambling. 
There shall be no gambling, betting, games of chance, punch boards, vending machines, slot machines, pinball machines, lotteries, or tickets of chance therein or the operation of any schemes for hazarding money or any other thing of value in any licensee's place of business or any room adjoining the same, owned, leased, or controlled by the licensee; provided, however, that the sale of state lottery tickets in compliance with O.C.G.A. § 50-27-1 et seq., shall be permitted. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(16), 32-205(23); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(16), 32-205(23)) 
Secs. 6-115—6-141. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - DENIAL OF LICENSE 

Sec. 6-142. - Grounds. 
(a)  The board of commissioners, in its discretion, may consider any and all relevant and extenuating circumstances which may reflect favorably or unfavorably on the applicant, application or the proposed location of the business. If, in the judgment of the board of commissioners, circumstances are such that the granting, suspension or revocation of the license would or would not be in the best interest of the general public, then such circumstances may be grounds for the denial of the application. 
(b)  Any misstatement, false statement, or concealment of fact in the application shall be grounds for the denial of the application for license issuance or revocation of the license issued and shall make the applicant liable to prosecution for perjury under the laws of the state. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(L), (M), 32-205(6)(G), (22); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(L), (M), 32-205(6)(G), (22)) 
Sec. 6-143. - Notice of denial. 
The board of commissioners shall give notice in writing to the applicant of any decision to grant or deny an application. The notice shall give the reason for the decision. Notice shall be given by personal service or by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(6)(I); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(6)(I)) 
Sec. 6-144. - Denial hearing. 
(a)  Whenever the board of commissioners shall deny an application for a package license or pouring license, the applicant shall have ten days following the date of receipt of such notice of the denial to request a hearing before the board. If a hearing is requested, the following information shall be given to the applicant, in writing, by personal service or by certified mail, return receipt requested, at least ten days prior to the hearing date: 
(1)  The date, time and location of the hearing, said hearing date not to be more than 20 days from the date of said written notice; 
(2)  A written statement of the reason for the proposed denial of the application; 
(3)  A list of witnesses, if any, the board of commissioners expects to testify or offer evidence in favor of the denial of the application; and 
(4)  Notice of the applicant's right to attend the hearing, to present evidence and testimony, to assert any defense of the application, to confront and cross examine anyone who would testify in favor of denial of application and to have an attorney present to represent the applicant. 
(b)  Any decision denying an application shall set forth the reason for such action in writing, which shall be delivered by regular mail to the applicant's address set forth in the application. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(N), 32-205(6)(J); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(N), 32-205(6)(J); Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), §§ 1, 2) 
Secs. 6-145—6-171. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - TRANSFERABILITY OF LICENSE 

Sec. 6-172. - Transferability. 
(a)  Except as otherwise stated in this section, no package or pouring license shall be transferable or assignable to any person or other location, and in the event that a licensed business is sold or closed, it shall be the duty of the licensee to immediately surrender said license to the board of commissioners. Under no circumstances will the license fee be refunded to the holder. 
(b)  All holders of licenses issued under this section shall, within six months after the issuance of such license, open for business the establishment referred to in the license. Failure to open the licensed establishment within such period shall serve as a forfeiture and cancellation of the unused license and no refund of the license fee shall be made to the license holder. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(13), 32-205(7); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(13), 32-205(7)) 
Secs. 6-173—6-197. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 7. - DUTIES OF LICENSEE 

Sec. 6-198. - Management and operation. 
The licensee shall be responsible for the management and operation of the business for which the license is granted and shall be responsible for all violations of this chapter by the licensee's agents and employees. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(4)(G), 32-205(6)(L); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(4)(G), 32-205(6)(L)) 
Sec. 6-199. - Purchase of malt beverages and wine. 
No licensee shall buy or arrange to buy or in any way cause the transfer of any malt beverages and/or wine except from a licensed wholesaler. A licensee under this chapter shall take delivery only at the licensed place of business from a licensed wholesaler or licensed common carrier acting for a licensed wholesaler. A licensee shall comply with all other requirements, including, without limitation, those set forth at Chapters 560-2 (Ga. Comp Rules and Regs. 560-2-1 et seq., Alcohol and Tobacco Tax Division) and 560-8 (Ga. Comp. Rules and Regs. 560-8-1 et seq., Alcohol and Tobacco Tax Division—Malt Beverages, Wine, Tobacco) of the Georgia Administrative Code, as well as the rules and regulations of the state department of revenue. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(7)(D), 32-204(31), 32-205(44), 32-205(46); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(7)(D), 32-204(31), 32-205(44), 32-205(46)) 
Sec. 6-200. - Inventory of malt beverage and wine. 
A licensee shall keep no inventory or stock of malt beverages and/or wine at any place except the licensed place of business, and within the licensed place of business the storage area for malt beverages and/or wine shall be immediately adjacent to and attached to the retail area or area of consumption. No licensee shall enter into any type of arrangement whereby malt beverages and/or wine ordered by the licensee are stored by a licensed wholesaler. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(7)(E), (33), 32-205(45); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(7)(E), (33), 32-205(45)) 
Sec. 6-201. - Display of license. 
A license issued under this chapter shall be displayed prominently at all times on the premises for which it was issued. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(8), 32-205(25); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(8), 32-205(25)) 
Sec. 6-202. - Condition of premises. 
(a)  All premises used for the sale and/or consumption of malt beverages and/or wine, and/or for the storage of malt beverages and/or wine, shall be kept in a sanitary condition and shall be kept in full compliance with the regulations of the county health department. 
(b)  All licensed premises shall be subject to inspection by the health department, all county fire departments, the building inspector, and all authorized law or code enforcement officers to determine if the premises are in compliance with all county, state and federal rules, regulations, laws and codes. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(23), 32-205(33); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(23), 32-205(33)) 
Sec. 6-203. - Telephone. 
A licensee shall maintain on the premises at all times a telephone in good working order. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(7)(F), 32-205(34); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(7)(F), 32-205(34)) 
Sec. 6-204. - Violent or disorderly history. 
It shall be unlawful for any licensee to knowingly allow any person with a criminal record for violence or disorder to frequent the licensed premises or loiter on the premises. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(7)(G), 32-205(27); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(7)(G), 32-205(27)) 
Sec. 6-205. - Prostitution. 
It shall be unlawful for any licensee to knowingly allow any person to frequent the licensed premises for the purpose of soliciting prostitution. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(7)(H), 32-205(28); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(7)(H), 32-205(28)) 
Sec. 6-206. - Police reports. 
It shall be unlawful for any licensee to fail to report to the police at the earliest possible time any known incident of a criminal nature that occur on the licensed premises. It shall be unlawful for any licensee to willfully withhold from the police any information pertaining to any crime that may have occurred on the licensed premises. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(7)(I), 32-205(29); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(7)(I), 32-205(29)) 
Sec. 6-207. - Criminal acts. 
It shall be unlawful for any licensee to knowingly allow any criminal act to be committed on the licensed premises. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(7)(J); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(7)(J)) 
Sec. 6-208. - Compliance with laws. 
In addition to the rules and regulations set out in this chapter, each licensee under this chapter shall comply with all statutory laws of the state, all federal statutory laws, and all rules and regulations of the state revenue commissioner relating to the sale and distribution of malt beverages and/or wine in the state; and any violation of same shall subject said licensee to suspension or revocation of his or her license and also may subject said licensee to criminal prosecution by the proper authority as provided by law and the ordinances of the county. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(17); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(17)) 
Sec. 6-209. - Production of records. 
In conjunction with any license application or any license issued under the terms hereof, or in conjunction with the revocation, suspension or cancellation of any license or in conjunction with any of the hearings contemplated by this chapter, or in conjunction with the payment or nonpayment of any excise tax levied or to be collected hereunder, the board of commissioners shall have the right to subpoena all or any part of the records, books, documents, reports or invoices of any applicant or licensee. Said subpoena right shall be had for the purposes of auditing the records of such applicant or licensee, securing compliance by such licensee with the provisions of this chapter, proving or disproving violation of any part of this chapter by any licensee, or to show payment or nonpayment of any taxes, fees, charges or the like due hereunder. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(22), 32-205(21); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(22), 32-205(21)) 
Sec. 6-210. - Copy of chapter. 
All licensees shall keep a copy of this chapter on the licensed premises and shall instruct any person working there about compliance with the terms hereof. Each licensee and the licensee's agents selling packaged malt beverages and/or wine, or selling for consumption on the premises malt beverages and/or wine, shall at all times be familiar with the terms hereof. The licensee shall be held responsible for any acts of the licensee's agents and employees which are in violation of this chapter, the statutory laws of the state, and/or the rules and regulations of the state revenue commissioner. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(26), 32-205(19); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(26), 32-205(19)) 
Sec. 6-211. - Posting of warnings. 
The licensee shall post in a conspicuous place in his or her establishment a sign printed in letters at least four inches high reading as follows: "SALE OF BEER AND WINE TO PERSONS UNDER 21 YEARS OF AGE STRICTLY PROHIBITED." The licensee shall also post in a conspicuous place in the licensed premises a sign printed in letters at least four inches high reading as follows: "WARNING: DRINKING BEER AND WINE DURING PREGNANCY CAN CAUSE BIRTH DEFECTS." 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(27), 32-205(13); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(27), 32-205(13); Ord. No. 2012-003, § 1(exh. A), 10-2-2012) 
Sec. 6-212. - Prohibited sales. 
No licensee nor any agent or employee of a licensee shall furnish, sell or offer to sell any malt beverage and/or wine to any person who is confined in any jail, penal institution, correctional facility, prison camp, penitentiary or other lawful place of confinement, or to any person who is a patient or inmate of the Central State Hospital, or to any person who is noticeably intoxicated, or is of unsound mind, or is a habitual drunkard whose intemperate habits are known to the licensee or the agent or employee. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(28), 32-205(14); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(28), 32-205(14)) 
Sec. 6-213. - Lock and key. 
All malt beverages and/or wine shall be under lock or fully covered by opaque material during those hours when their sale is not permitted except in the event of an emergency or under the direction of a law enforcement official, county official or his or her designate. All malt beverages and/or wine owned or possessed contrary to the provisions of this chapter are hereby declared to be contraband and shall be seized by the proper authorities. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(29), 32-205(40); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(29), 32-205(40)) 
Sec. 6-214. - Containers. 
It shall be unlawful for licensees or their agents or employees to add to the contents of a container or to refill empty containers or in any manner to misrepresent the quantity, quality or brand name of any malt beverage and/or wine. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(30), 32-205(32); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(30), 32-205(32)) 
Secs. 6-215—6-236. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 8. - EMPLOYEES 

Sec. 6-237. - Employee list; employment requirements. 
(a)  Every licensee under this chapter shall maintain at all times on the premises for which the license has been issued a list of all persons currently employed by such licensee at such premises, which list shall show the current full legal name, alias, date of birth, current address, current home telephone number and social security number of each employee. 
(b)  The employee list shall be available during reasonable hours for inspection by any law enforcement officer or county official or his or her designee. If so required by such person, an employee must submit to a fingerprint identification and criminal history check. Every licensee shall cause each of the licensee's employees during the hours of his or her employment to be identified by a conspicuous label or badge upon which shall appear the employee's first name. 
(c)  No person under 21 years of age shall be employed in any capacity in any place of business licensed under this section. No holder of a pouring license shall employ, require or permit a person under 21 years of age to sell or take orders for malt beverages and/or wine. However, persons under 21 years of age who are employed in supermarkets, convenience stores, breweries and drugstores that are licensed to engage in the retail sale of malt beverages and/or wine in unbroken packages and not for consumption on the premises may sell or handle malt beverages and/or wine which are sold pursuant to and in compliance with this chapter. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for any licensee to employ on the premises any person who, in the preceding ten years, has been convicted of a felony or misdemeanor involving moral turpitude in the state or who has been convicted of a crime outside the state which would be a felony or misdemeanor involving moral turpitude in the state. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(25), 32-205(36); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(25), 32-205(36)) 
Secs. 6-238—6-267. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 9. - MINORS 

Sec. 6-268. - Sale or possession of malt beverages and/or wine prohibited; exception. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for a minor to attempt to purchase malt beverages and/or wine or for any other person to purchase malt beverages and/or wine for a minor. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for a minor to exhibit fake, forged, or borrowed credentials in an effort to obtain malt beverages and/or wine to which the minor is not legally entitled. 
(c)  No person engaged in the business regulated hereunder shall make or permit to be made any sale of malt beverages and/or wine to minors. 
(d)  No person shall allow anyone under 21 years of age to loiter about the premises of the licensee or possess any alcoholic beverage. This provision shall not apply to employees over the age of 18 years eligible for subject employment under the laws of the state. 
(e)  Any violations of the provisions of this division shall constitute a misdemeanor and the offender, upon being found guilty, shall be punishable as for a misdemeanor, and by possible loss of license and fine. 
(f)  The prohibition contained in this subsection shall not apply with respect to the sale, purchase or possession of malt beverages and/or wine for consumption: 
(1)  For medical purposes pursuant to a prescription of a physician duly authorized to practice medicine in the state; 
(2)  At a religious ceremony; or 
(3)  In the minor's home with parental consent. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(18), 32-205(31); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(18), 32-205(31)) 
Secs. 6-269—6-299. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 10. - VIOLATION AND DUE PROCESS 

Sec. 6-300. - Violations. 
(a)  Any violation of one or more provisions of this chapter shall be punishable pursuant to section 1-9, and shall be tried in the magistrate court as set forth in section 1-10. 
(b)  In addition to any punishment for violating this chapter, any such violation may subject a licensee to the revocation or suspension of his or her license, as set forth in sections 6-301 and 6-302. 
(1)  Any revocation or suspension based upon a violation of this chapter will subject the licensee to a reinstatement fee between $500.00 and $1,000.00, to be determined in the discretion of the board. 
a.  This reinstatement fee is non-refundable and must be paid prior to the reinstatement of any license issued under this chapter. 
b.  No new license shall be issued to a licensee whose previous license was revoked or suspended until the reinstatement fee is paid. 
c.  Payment of the non-refundable reinstatement fee does not guarantee the reinstatement or issuance of a license, but is instead a condition precedent to the consideration of reinstatement or issuance by the board. 
(2)  In addition to any other punishments or civil penalties set forth herein, any revocation or suspension based upon a violation of this chapter, may subject a licensee to the forfeiture of all stock of malt beverages and wine. 
(3)  The following suspension and revocation guidelines apply to a licensee who violates this chapter by selling or allowing the sale at his or her establishment of beer and/or wine to an ineligible individual under this chapter (including but not limited to a minor), sells during hours and/or days on which sales of beer and/or wine are prohibited under this chapter, and/or sells without a valid license, whether suspended, revoked, or not yet issued: 
a.  For a first offense within the previous five years, a 30-day suspension of his or her license and a reinstatement fee of $500.00. 
b.  For a second or subsequent offense within five years of a first offense, the revocation of his or her license for the remainder of the year, a reinstatement fee of $1,000.00, and forfeiture of all stock in malt beverages and wine. 
c.  These guidelines in subsections i. and ii. above are those a licensee can expect to receive as a minimum, although the board will make the final decision in each instance and has the right to impose differing suspensions, revocations, and reinstatement fees. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(19), 32-205(47); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(19), 32-205(47); Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), §§ 1, 2) 
Sec. 6-301. - Suspension or revocation of license. 
(a)  No person shall engage in the package sale of malt beverages and/or wine, or the sale of the same for consumption on the premises, in the unincorporated areas of the county without first complying with the rules and requirements set out in this chapter. Any license issued hereunder shall be subject to suspension or revocation upon any of the following grounds: 
(1)  The making of any false statement on an application for a license issued hereunder; 
(2)  A violation of the rules and regulations set out in this section and/or the laws and/or regulations of the United States and/or the state and/or the county; 
(3)  The failure to have the financial responsibility upon which issuance of the license was conditioned; 
(4)  Default in any obligation, of any kind whatsoever, lawfully owing to the county; 
(5)  Cancellation, suspension or revocation of a state malt beverage and/or wine license; 
(6)  Any violation of this section; or 
(7)  For any other legal and sufficient cause. 
(b)  In addition to the above-listed grounds for suspension or revocation, any pouring license issued hereunder shall be subject to suspension or revocation for a failure to meet the food/alcohol percentage requirement set forth in the definition of restaurant in section 6-2 in any one calendar quarter. 
(c)  Any action taken by the board of commissioners to suspend or revoke a license issued hereunder shall not preclude and may be in addition to any fines and prosecution by a proper authority as provided by the laws and/or ordinances of the county, the state, and/or the United States and forfeiture of all stock of malt beverage and wine. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(20), 32-205(42); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(20), 32-205(42)) 
Sec. 6-302. - Due process. 
(a)  Whenever the board of commissioners wishes to take any action to suspend or revoke any license issued hereunder, the board shall provide ten days' written notice, by personal service or certified mail, return receipt requested, to the licensee prior to taking such action. The notice shall set forth the reasons for such action. The licensee shall have ten days from the date of receipt of such notification of such action (as set forth on the aforesaid receipt) to request a hearing before the board. Said notification shall be in writing and shall be delivered to the board by hand delivery or by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(b)  If a hearing is requested, the following information shall be given to the licensee, in writing, by regular mail to the licensee's last known address, at least ten days prior to the hearing date: 
(1)  A written copy of all charges or reasons for the proposed suspension or revocation; 
(2)  The date, time and location of the hearing, said hearing date to be not more than 20 days from the date of said written notice; 
(3)  A list of witnesses, if any, the board expects to testify or offer evidence in favor of the suspension or revocation; and 
(4)  Notice of the licensee's right to attend the hearing, to present evidence and testimony, to assert any defense, to confront and cross examine opposing witnesses, and to have an attorney present to represent the licensee. 
(c)  All decisions suspending or revoking a license shall set forth the reason for such action in writing, and shall be delivered to the licensee at his or her last known address by regular mail. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-204(21), 32-205(43); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-204(21), 32-205(43); Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), §§ 1, 2) 
Secs. 6-303—6-322. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PACKAGE SALE OF MALT BEVERAGES AND WINE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Governing authority of county has power to locally regulate, license, and tax the manufacturing, distribution and selling of malt beverages, O.C.G.A. §§ 3-5-40 et seq., 3-5-80 et seq.; governing authority of county has power to locally regulate, license, and tax the manufacturing, distribution and selling of wine, O.C.G.A. §§ 3-6-40 et seq., 3-6-60 et seq. 

Sec. 6-323. - Off-premises consumption. 
Malt beverages and/or wine sold pursuant to a package license granted under this chapter will be for consumption only off the premises of the licensee. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(3); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(3)) 
Sec. 6-324. - Bond requirement. 
Before any package license is granted, the applicant must post with the board of commissioners, along with the application, a cash bond or performance bond with an insurance company as surety. Said bond shall require the faithful observance and performance by the licensee of the rules and regulations contained in this section. Upon the violation of this section, or any part thereof, the amount of the bond to be forfeited will be determined by the seriousness of the violation as determined by the board. Said bond is to be approved by the board and shall be properly executed. Said bond shall be in the amount of $2,500.00 for a wholesale permit and $500.00 for a retail license. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(5)(d); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(5)(d)) 
Sec. 6-325. - Annual license fee. 
The annual fee for a license shall be $500.00 per annum and shall be paid after acceptance and approval of the application by the board of commissioners, but prior to the issuance of such license. The fee shall be paid either in cash or by bank certified check. All licenses shall expire on December 31 of the year for which they were granted. No license fee shall be prorated. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(6); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(6)) 
Sec. 6-326. - Regulations. 
(a)  No licensee shall sell or deliver any malt beverages and/or wine to any person except in the licensee's place of business. A licensee shall be permitted to load purchased goods in a customer's vehicle when the sale physically takes place and monies have been exchanged inside the place of business. A licensee may have a drive-in window and may deliver packaged malt beverages and/or wine through such window. Said drive-in window must be visible from the nearest street. "Curb service" type sales and sales to customers in vehicles parked in the parking area of the place of business are prohibited. 
(b)  No licensee shall furnish, sell or offer for sale any malt beverages and/or wine at any times except: 
(1)  Between 6:00 a.m. and 11:45 p.m. on Mondays through Saturday; and 
(2)  Between 12:30 p.m. and 11:30 p.m. on Sundays. 
(c)  No person shall sell or possess for the purpose of sale, any malt beverages and/or wine where such person does not have a license from the board of commissioners to sell or possess for sale such beverages and/or wine. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(7), (32); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(7), (32); Ord. No. 2012-003, § 1(exh. A), 10-2-2012) 
Sec. 6-327. - Location and relocation. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-4-49, no license shall be granted to any person authorizing the location of a new retail package liquor licensed place of business or the relocation of an existing retail package liquor licensed place of business engaged in the retail package sales of distilled spirits within 500 yards of any other business licensed to sell package liquor at retail, as measured by the most direct route of travel on the ground. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(4)(C); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(4)(C)) 
Sec. 6-328. - Wholesale permits. 
Any wholesale distributor in malt beverages and wine licensed by the state or the agent of such licensed wholesale distributor may be granted a permit to distribute such malt beverages and wine in the county, upon application for such permit to the clerk, and upon the presentation of evidence satisfactory to said county that the applicant understands and will comply with all terms and conditions and provisions of the chapter governing the package sale of malt beverages and wine in the county, as said chapter may be amended, including, but not limited to, those under which malt beverages and wine licenses are issued, and upon payment of an annual fee of $100.00 for malt beverage wholesale distributors pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-5-43, a fee of $500.00 for wine wholesale distributors and a fee of $600.00 for wholesale distributors of both beer and wine; provided, however, that malt beverage wholesale distributors who have their principal place of business in the county shall pay an annual fee of $2,500.00. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(9); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(9)) 
Sec. 6-329. - Malt beverage taxes; distributor reports. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-5-80 and O.C.G.A. § 3-5-81, there is hereby levied upon wholesale malt beverages distributors a tax on malt beverages as follows: 
(1)  Malt beverages, commonly known as tap or draft beer, sold in or from a barrel or bulk container, shall be at a rate of $6.00 on each container sold containing not more than 15 1/2 gallons, and a proportional tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 15 1/2 gallons. 
(2)  When malt beverages are sold in bottles, cans, or other containers, except barrel or bulk containers, a tax of $0.05 per 12 ounces and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 12 ounces. 
Each wholesale distributor shall furnish to the board of commissioners a report itemizing all purchase invoices for malt beverages sold to each licensee in the county, on or before the tenth day of the month following such purchase. Said invoices shall show the amount of excise tax paid. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(10); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(10)) 
Sec. 6-330. - Wine taxes; exemptions; reports. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-6-60, there is hereby levied on the first sale or use of wine by the package a tax of $0.22 per liter and a proportionate tax at the time rate on all fractional parts of a liter. Each month the first purchaser or user shall furnish to the board of commissioners a report itemizing each first purchase or use during the month. The report shall be furnished before the tenth day of the month following the month reported. The report shall show the amount of excise tax paid during the reported month. Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-6-70 and O.C.G.A. § 3-6-71, no tax shall be levied by the board with respect to: 
(1)  Wine sold to and used by established and recognized churches and synagogues for use in sacramental services only; 
(2)  Any sale of wine which is exempt from taxation by the state or under the Constitution of the United States; 
(3)  Wine sold to persons outside this state for resale or consumption outside this state; or 
(4)  Wines which contain less than one-half of one percent alcohol by volume. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(11); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(11)) 
Sec. 6-331. - Financial responsibility. 
Any applicant for a license must show financial responsibility to the satisfaction of the board of commissioners. Financial statements must be submitted with each completed application as prescribed by the board. Any applicant who becomes licensed must maintain a minimum of $1,000.00 stock of goods while said license is held by said licensee. The stock shall be subject to inventory audit at the discretion of the board. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(12); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(12)) 
Sec. 6-332. - Transportation. 
(a)  All malt beverages transported or delivered to a licensee shall be packaged in the following manner, to-wit: seven-ounce, eight-ounce or 12-ounce sealed containers packaged four, six or 12 per package; 16-ounce sealed containers packaged six per package; 24-ounce sealed containers packaged only by the full case; 32-ounce sealed containers packaged only by the case; and draft beer in sealed containers which contain one-half barrel (15 1/2 gallons), one-quarter barrel (7 3/4 gallons) or any other size as draft beer is normally sold, transported and delivered in sealed containers within the state. 
(b)  All wine transported or delivered to a licensee shall be packaged in containers specified in the Standards of Fill for Wine prescribed by the Department of the Treasury of the United States for wines shipped in interstate commerce. The federal regulations relating to Standards of Fill for Wine are adopted and incorporated by reference into this subsection. Wines manufactured and produced in the state shall be exempt from the provisions of this subsection to the extent that they are exempted from the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 3-6-28, as amended from time to time. 
(Code 2000, § 32-204(14); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-204(14)) 
Secs. 6-333—6-352. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - SALE OF MALT BEVERAGES AND WINE FOR CONSUMPTION ON THE PREMISES[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Governing authority of county has power to locally regulate, license, and tax the manufacturing, distribution and selling of malt beverages, O.C.G.A. §§ 3-5-40 et seq., 3-5-80 et seq.; governing authority of county has power to locally regulate, license, and tax the manufacturing, distribution and selling of wine, O.C.G.A. §§ 3-6-40 et seq., 3-6-60 et seq.; local government may authorize issuance license to sell distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on premises where sold, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-90 et seq. 

Sec. 6-353. - Unlawful sales without license. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or offer to sell any malt beverages and/or wine for consumption on the premises without first complying with the rules and regulations set forth in this chapter. It shall be unlawful in any case for any person to sell or offer to sell any malt beverage and/or wine for consumption on the premises without first complying with this chapter. It shall be unlawful in any case for any person to sell or offer to sell any distilled spirits for consumption on the premises. 
(b)  A bed-and-breakfast may serve wine and/or malt beverages to its overnight guests without a license under this chapter so long as: 
(1)  The cost of the guests' lodging and meals exceeds the cost of alcohol provided; and 
(2)  No alcohol is provided to guests not staying at the bed-and-breakfast. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(3); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(3)) 
State Law reference— Unlawful to knowingly or intentionally allow drinking of contents of alcoholic beverage on premises where sold without a license for consumption on the premises, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-26. 
Sec. 6-354. - Bond requirement. 
Before any pouring license is granted, the applicant must post with the board of commissioners, along with the application, a cash bond or performance bond with an insurance company as surety. Said bond shall require the faithful observance and performance by the licensee of the rules and regulations contained in this article. Upon the violation of this article, or any part thereof, the amount of the bond to be forfeited will be determined by the seriousness of the violation as determined by the board. Said bond is to be approved by the board and shall be properly executed. Said bond shall be in the amount of $1,000.00 for a pouring license. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(4)(D); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(4)(D)) 
Sec. 6-355. - Additional application requirements. 
(a)  No malt beverages and/or wine shall be sold by the drink for consumption on the premises except under a pouring license granted by the board of commissioners. Application for such license may be made only on behalf of restaurants and private clubs located within the unincorporated areas of the county, and shall be made on forms provided by the board. 
(b)  Any application for a pouring license hereunder for a private club shall contain certified copies of all documents necessary for the board to ascertain that the applicant meets the requirements of a private club as defined in this chapter. 
(c)  All applications for pouring licenses submitted by applicants who are operating a place of business under a preexisting license issued pursuant to this article shall be approved or disapproved at the regularly called December meeting of the board. 
(d)  All applicants for a pouring license must show financial responsibility. The board may require all applicants to provide financial statements and other evidence of financial responsibility in conjunction with the application. The form of the application shall be set by the board, and must be fully completed by the applicant and filed by the applicant with the clerk of the board. 
(e)  All pouring license applicants must be persons operating at the proposed licensed place of business a "restaurant" or "private club" as defined in this chapter. No lounges shall be permitted. 
(Code 2000, §§ 32-205(4), (6); Ord. of 11-2-2004, §§ 32-205(4), (6)) 
Sec. 6-356. - Reports. 
(a)  Each licensee under this section shall, as a condition of maintaining such license, file with the clerk within 30 days after the end of each calendar quarter: 
(1)  A sworn statement of the licensee's sales during the preceding calendar quarter on forms approved by the county. The forms for such quarterly verified statements shall reflect the licensee's gross dollar sales amount for total sales for the applicable calendar quarter, the gross dollar sales amount for malt beverages and wine for the applicable calendar quarter, and gross dollar sales amount for food items for the applicable calendar quarter. 
(2)  Certified copies of the licensee's state department of revenue sales and use tax monthly reports as filed with the state department of revenue for each month during the respective calendar quarter. 
(b)  Any sale of a food or beverage containing any malt beverage and/or wine shall be deemed to be a sale solely of a malt beverage and/or wine, and such sale shall not be included as a food sale in the quarterly reports. The fact that the sale of food during any calendar quarter exceeds by three times the sales of malt beverages and/or wine shall not be conclusive that the licensee is meeting the requirements of operating a restaurant as defined in this chapter. However, the failure of the food sales to so exceed by three times the sale of malt beverages and wine shall be prima facie evidence that the establishment is not meeting the definition of a restaurant. 
(c)  The quarterly statements shall be confidential in nature and shall not be open for public inspection except as otherwise required by law. Said forms shall be used solely by the county manager for determination of whether or not the licensee remains qualified to hold a pouring license. Failure to timely file such statements shall be a violation of this article punishable by a fine of up to $500.00, and cause for suspension or revocation of the license granted under this article. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(12); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(12)) 
Sec. 6-357. - On-premises consumption. 
No licensee may sell malt beverages and/or wine in unbroken packages or in any quantity for other than consumption on the premises. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(16); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(16)) 
Sec. 6-358. - Annual license fees. 
The annual fee for a malt beverage and wine pouring license shall be $1,000.00 per annum per requested license and shall be paid after acceptance and approval of the application by the board of commissioners but prior to the issuance of such license. The fee shall be paid either in cash or by bank certified check. All licenses shall expire on December 31 of the year for which they were granted. No license fee shall be prorated. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(17); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(17)) 
Sec. 6-359. - Malt beverage taxes. 
(a)  Where malt beverages are sold in or from a barrel or bulk container as tap or draft beer, there is levied a state excise tax on malt beverages of $10.00 on each container sold containing not more than 31 gallons, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 31 gallons. 
(b)  Where malt beverages are sold in bottles, cans or other containers other than barrels or other bulk containers, a state excise tax of $0.045 per 12 ounces shall be collected, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts shall be collected. 
(c)  There is levied a state excise tax on all such beverages in excess of 576 ounces or two standard cases of 12-ounce size or the equivalent thereof or one 7.75-gallon keg or barrel of such beverages, said tax being levied at the rate of taxation of $0.045 per 12 ounces. 
(d)  The board of commissioners shall impose an excise tax, in addition to the excise taxes levied by the state, as follows: 
(1)  Where malt beverages, commonly known as tap or draft beer, are sold in or from a barrel or bulk container, a tax of $6.00 on each container sold containing not more that 15 1/2 gallons and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 15 1/2 gallons; 
(2)  Where malt beverages are sold in bottles, cans, or other containers, except barrel or bulk containers, a tax of $0.05 per 12 ounces and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 12 ounces. 
(e)  It shall be unlawful and a violation of this article for any retail dealer to possess, own, hold, store, display, or sell any malt beverages on which such taxes have not been paid. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(18)(A); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(18)(A)) 
Sec. 6-360. - Wine taxes. 
(a)  There is levied and imposed on the first sale, use or final delivery within this state of all table wines a state excise tax in the amount of $0.11 per liter and a proportional tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
(b)  There is imposed upon the importation for use, consumption, or final delivery into this state of all table wines a state import tax in the amount of $0.29 per liter and a proportional tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
(c)  There is levied and imposed on the first sale, use or final delivery within this state of all dessert wines a state excise tax in the amount of $0.27 per liter and a proportional tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
(d)  There is imposed upon the importation for use, consumption, or final delivery into this state of all dessert wines a state import tax in the amount of $0.40 per liter and a proportional tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
(e)  There is hereby levied by the board of commissioners an excise tax on the first sale or use of wine by the package at the rate of $0.22 per liter and a proportional tax at the same rate for any fractional parts of a liter. 
(f)  The taxes imposed on wine shall not be levied on any wine sold to established and recognized churches and synagogues for use in sacramental services only, or for any wine exempt from taxation under the Constitution of the United States, or for any wine sold to persons for resale or consumption outside this state. 
(g)  It shall be unlawful and a violation of this article for any retail dealer to possess, own, hold, store, display, or sell any wine on which such taxes have not been paid. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(18)(B); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(18)(B)) 
Sec. 6-361. - Soliciting. 
No retail licensee shall require, permit, suffer, encourage, or induce any employee or person to solicit in the licensed premises for himself or for any person other than the patron and guests of the patron, the purchase by the patron of any malt beverage and/or wine, or money with which to purchase the same; nor shall any licensee pay a commission or any other compensation to any person frequenting his or her establishment or to his or her agent or manager to solicit for himself or herself or for others, the purchase by the patron of malt beverage and/or wine. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(25); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(25)) 
Sec. 6-362. - Delivery. 
It shall be unlawful for any licensee to make delivery of any malt beverage and/or wine except inside of the premises or area licensed for the sale thereof. It shall be unlawful for any such licensee to sell malt beverages and/or wine for consumption off the premises. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(26); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(26)) 
Sec. 6-363. - Promotions. 
No licensee or employee or agent of a licensee shall engage in any of the following practices in connection with the sale or other disposition of malt beverages and/or wine: 
(1)  The giving away of any ticket, token or any other item that can be exchanged for any malt beverage and/or wine upon the purchase of any other malt beverage and/or wine; 
(2)  The sale of two or more malt beverages and/or wine for a single price, or the sale of one serving of malt beverage and/or wine with a ticket, token or any other items redeemable for a subsequent serving of malt beverage and/or wine. Also prohibited hereunder is the sale of all such beverages a customer can or desires to drink at a single price. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(37); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(37)) 
Sec. 6-364. - Prohibited acts. 
No licensee shall authorize or permit any patron or customer to bring onto the premises one or more alcoholic beverages purchased elsewhere, nor shall any such licensee authorize or permit any patron or customer to take out of the premises one or more alcoholic beverages. No licensee shall authorize or permit any patron or customer to bring or carry any deadly weapon or firearm on the premises except a law enforcement officer or other person authorized by federal or state law to bring or carry any deadly weapon or firearm on the premises, nor shall the licensee act as a keeper, bailee or custodian of any kind of deadly weapon or firearm for any customer or patron. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(38); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(38)) 
Sec. 6-365. - Clearing service areas. 
All licensees shall remove or cause to be removed from the area of the premises utilized by the customers or patrons all malt beverages and/or wine within one-half hour after the time for last call specified in section 6-366. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(39); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(39)) 
Sec. 6-366. - Hours. 
No malt beverage and/or wine may be served before 8:00 a.m. or after 11:45 p.m., Mondays through Saturdays. Malt beverages and beer may not be served on Sundays. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205(41); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205(41); Ord. No. 2012-003, § 1(exh. A), 10-2-2012) 
Secs. 6-367—6-390. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE CATERING[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference— Local government has authority to issue an off-premises license allowing alcoholic beverage caterer to sell malt beverages or wine by the drink off premises and in connection with an authorized catered function, O.C.G.A. § 3-11-1 et seq. 

Sec. 6-391. - Off-premises alcoholic beverage catering license. 
(a)  Any licensed alcoholic beverage caterer who holds a valid license from the county to sell: 
(1)  At a fixed location within the county, malt beverages or wine by the drink for consumption on the premises; or 
(2)  By the package for consumption off the premises; 
may be issued an off-premises license which authorizes such licensed alcoholic beverage caterer to distribute malt beverages and/or wine at an authorized catered function. 
(b)  Application for an off-premises license as provided herein shall be made to the county clerk upon forms to be prepared and approved by the board of commissioners. Applications will be decided according to the same rules and guidelines set forth in this chapter. 
(c)  The annual fee for an alcoholic beverage caterer's license shall be $100.00 annually for each licensed location. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205A(2); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205A(2)) 
Sec. 6-392. - Event permits. 
(a)  Alcoholic beverage caterer licensed by the county. In order to distribute malt beverages and/or wine at an authorized catered function, an alcoholic beverage caterer licensed by the county shall be required to: 
(1)  Apply for an event permit. The application shall include: 
a.  The name of the alcoholic beverage caterer, including the name of the specific representative of the caterer who will be responsible for, and present at, the catered function; 
b.  The date of the event; 
c.  The address of the event; 
d.  The time of the event; 
e.  The licensed alcoholic beverage caterer's license number; and 
f.  The name, address and phone number of the host of the catered function. 
No event permit fee shall be charged. 
(2)  Provide satisfactory reports to the state revenue commissioner on forms provided by that department, stating the quantity of any and all alcoholic beverages transported from the licensee's primary premises to the location of the authorized catered function and such other information as required by the commissioner. 
(3)  Maintain original local event permits and documents required by the state revenue department in the vehicle transporting the alcoholic beverages to the catered function at all times. 
(4)  Comply with all laws and ordinances regulating the sale and distribution of alcoholic beverages, and no permit will be issued to any alcohol beverage caterer on probation or with a suspended license. 
(b)  Alcoholic beverage caterer licensed by other jurisdictions. In order to distribute malt beverages and/or wine at an authorized catered function, an alcoholic beverage caterer licensed by a subdivision of the state other than the county shall be required to: 
(1)  Apply for an event permit. The application shall include: 
a.  The name of the alcoholic beverage caterer, including the name of the specific representative of the caterer who will be responsible for, and present at, the catered function; 
b.  The date of the event; 
c.  The address of the event; 
d.  The time of the event; 
e.  The jurisdiction issuing the alcoholic beverage caterer's license; 
f.  The licensed alcoholic beverage caterer's license number; 
g.  A photocopy of the alcoholic beverage caterer's license; and 
h.  The name, address and phone number of the host of the catered function. 
(2)  Pay an event permit fee of $10.00; 
(3)  Pay local excise taxes that will be levied on the total quantity of alcoholic beverages brought into the county by the caterer, as calculated under this article, within 15 days of the conclusion of the catered event; 
(4)  Provide satisfactory reports to the state revenue commissioner on forms provided by that department, stating the quantity of any and all alcoholic beverages transported from the licensee's primary premises to the location of the authorized catered function and such other information as required by the commissioner; and 
(5)  Maintain original local event permits and documents required by the revenue department in the vehicle transporting the alcoholic beverages to the catered function at all times. 
(c)  Charitable organizations. 
(1)  Charitable organizations, as defined in this chapter, may serve malt beverages and/or wine at authorized catered functions without an alcoholic beverage catering license, so long as the qualified charitable organizations apply for an event permit. The application shall include: 
a.  The name of the charitable organization; 
b.  The name of the caterer; 
c.  The date of the event; 
d.  The address of the event; 
e.  The time of the event; and 
f.  The name, address and phone number of the host of the catered function. 
(2)  A charitable organization serving alcoholic beverages under this subsection is limited to 12 event permits per calendar year. 
(d)  Issuance of event permits. The issuance of event permits is an administrative function of the county, and the county is permitted under this article to request additional information from the licensed alcoholic beverage caterer and/or host of the catered event in deciding whether to issue an event permit. However, no event permit will be issued: 
(1)  Where the requirements set forth under subsection (a), (b) or (c) of this section have not been met; 
(2)  Where the host or the alcoholic beverage caterer has violated any of the prohibitions set forth in section 6-393; or 
(3)  To licensed alcoholic beverage caterers, where the total cost of alcohol at a catered event will exceed the total cost of food at an event. This subsection does not apply to qualified charitable organizations. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205A(3); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205A(3)) 
Sec. 6-393. - Violations. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for a food caterer to distribute or sell malt beverages and/or wine off the premises of the food caterer's business without a license issued pursuant to this section. This subsection shall not affect any other provisions of this chapter which may require a food caterer who has a license to sell alcoholic beverages on the premises of the food caterer's business. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for a licensed alcoholic beverage caterer licensed under this article to distribute malt beverages and/or wine off premises except in connection with an authorized catered function within the scope of the event permit for that function. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for anyone, including licensed alcoholic beverage caterers, to distribute distilled spirits in the unincorporated areas of the county. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for a licensed alcoholic beverage caterer to distribute malt beverages and/or wine during any of the following times: 
(1)  At any time on Sundays; 
(2)  At any time on Christmas Day; or 
(3)  At any time in violation of state law, state rules or regulations, local ordinances or regulations. 
(e)  It shall be unlawful for a licensed alcoholic beverage caterer to employ any person under 21 years of age who, in the course of such employment, would dispense, serve, sell, or handle alcoholic beverages. It is the intent of this subsection to prevent any person employed by such caterer, or any other employee, to knowingly violate any prohibitions contained in O.C.G.A. § 3-3-23, relating to furnishing alcoholic beverages to, and the purchase and possession of alcoholic beverages by, a person under 21 years of age. 
(f)  It shall be unlawful for anyone, including, but not limited to, hosts of catered functions and licensed alcoholic beverage caterers, to charge admission to a catered function. 
(g)  It shall be unlawful for anyone, including, but not limited to, hosts of catered functions and licensed alcoholic beverage caterers, to charge attendees at catered events for alcoholic beverages, directly or indirectly. 
(h)  Any person violating the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of up to $1,000.00 and/or imprisonment up to one year. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205A(4); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205A(4)) 
Sec. 6-394. - Exemptions. 
(a)  Charitable organizations (as defined in section 6-2) holding authorized catered functions may charge admission to catered alcohol events and may charge attendees for alcoholic beverages, so long as the money collected is used primarily for charitable purposes and not solely to defray the costs of the alcohol provided. 
(b)  Fundraisers for candidates for political office may accept contributions from attendees at authorized catered functions, so long as the contributions are primarily used for the candidates' political campaigns and not solely to defray the costs of the alcohol provided. 
(c)  Nothing contained in this section is intended to prohibit anyone from hosting private functions within the county where the host provides alcohol to guests free of charge. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205A(5); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205A(5)) 
Sec. 6-395. - Compliance with this chapter. 
In addition to the requirements set forth herein, all licensed alcoholic beverage caterers performing alcoholic beverage catering services in the county are required to comply with all of the provisions of article III of this chapter that are not inconsistent with this article. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205A(6); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205A(6)) 
Sec. 6-396. - State law. 
All licensed alcoholic beverage caterers performing alcoholic beverage catering services in the county are required to comply with all state laws, including but not limited to O.C.G.A. §§ 3-4-20 et seq., 3-5-20 et seq., 3-6-20 et seq., and 3-11-1 et seq., and all regulations promulgated by the state department of revenue, including but not limited to Ga. Admin. Code § 560-2-10 et seq. 
(Code 2000, § 32-205A(7); Ord. of 11-2-2004, § 32-205A(7)) 
Chapter 10 - ANIMALS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Animal control is a local home rule power, Ga. Const. art. IX, §§ I, III(a)(3). 

Sec. 10-1. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this chapter is to create the position of animal control officer; to establish his or her duties; to provide regulations for the vaccination of dogs; to provide for the confinement, disposition and humane disposal of dogs; to provide for regulating animals and fowl running at large; to provide for the classification and registration of dangerous animals, potentially dangerous animals and exotic animals in the county; to provide for requirements for possessing such animals or exotic animals; to provide grounds for the confiscation and disposition of such animals or exotic animals; to comply with the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 4-8-20 et seq.; and for other purposes. 
(Code 2000, § 30-101; Ord. of 2-5-2002, § 2(exh. B(30-101)); Ord. of 9-12-2006, § 30-101) 
Sec. 10-2. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Adequate food means palatable, noncontaminated, and nutritionally adequate food that is fed according to the species requirements or is fed as directed by a veterinarian. 
Adequate water means clean, fresh, potable water offered to animals at suitable intervals according to species or as directed by a veterinarian. 
Animal means any and all types of animals, both domesticated and wild. 
Animal control officer means an individual selected by the county pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 4-8-22 to aid in the administration and enforcement of this chapter. 
Animal establishment means any pet shop, grooming shop, animal auction, kennel, performing animal exhibition, or animal shelter, except this term shall not include veterinary medical facilities, licensed research facilities, facilities operated by government agencies, or licensed animal dealers regulated by the USDA. 
Animal shelter means a facility designated or recognized by the county for the purpose of impounding or caring for animals. 
At large means off the premises of the owner of the animal or fowl, and not under the immediate control of the owner. 
Board means the county board of commissioners. 
Business days means Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday, Thursday, and Friday. Saturdays, Sundays, and official federal, state and county holidays are not business days. 
Cat means small quadruped, of the feline family, typically domesticated. 
County manager means the individual so appointed to serve by the the county board of commissioners. 
Dangerous animal means any animal that: 
(1)  Inflicts a severe injury on a human being or other animal without provocation on public or private property at any time after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived; or 
(2)  Aggressively bites, attacks or endangers the safety of humans or other animals without provocation after the animal has been classified as a potentially dangerous animal and after the owner has been notified of such classification. 
Dead animal means any carcass or parts of a carcass of any animal. 
Dog means a common canine quadruped, mainly domesticated. 
Domesticated animal means those taxa of animals which have traditionally lived in a state of dependence on and under the dominion and control of man and have been kept as tame pets, raised as livestock, or used for commercial breeding purposes, including, but not limited to, dogs, cats, and poultry. Animals which live in a captive or tame state and which lack a genetic distinction from members of the same taxon living in the wild are presumptively wild animals. 
Equine means a horse, pony, mule, donkey, or hinny. 
Excessively loud and disturbing noise means continual repetitive noise which a person inside a residence can clearly hear and distinguish from the background ambient noise, and which can be ascertained and identified as to its nature and source. 
Exotic animal means any wild animal, wildlife, vertebrate or invertebrate recognized by the state as wild animal, wildlife, exotic or hybrid or regulated by state law in O.C.G.A. § 27-5-5 irrespective of its actual or asserted state of docility, domesticity, tameness or intended use and/or capable of causing severe injury by means of venoms, poisons, toxins, constriction or bite. The term "exotic animal" shall not include psittaciformes, ferrets, miniature pigs, hamsters, guinea pigs, gerbils, chinchillas, dogs, cats or llamas, any other animals recognized by the state as customarily and legally obtained and kept as a pet or snakes that are exotic animals and are recognized as pets by the state (boa, python, etc.) less than four feet in length. 
Feral means existing in a wild or untamed state, or having returned to an untamed state from domestication. 
Fowl means any and all fowl, domesticated and wild. 
Guard dog means any dog which has been trained to attack persons or other animals independently or upon verbal command and any dog which, while not so trained, is reasonably expected to perform as a guardian of property. 
Humane care means, but is not limited to, the provision of adequate heat, ventilation, sanitary shelter, and adequate food and adequate water, consistent with the normal requirements and feeding habits of the animal's size, species and breed. 
Inoculate means vaccination, by a state-licensed veterinarian, of a specified dose of antirabies vaccine to an animal, such vaccine having the U.S. government license number or approval stamped on the label of the vaccine container and having been approved by the state department of human resources. 
Kennel means an establishment for breeding, selling, training or boarding dogs or cats. 
Licensing authority means the county agency or designated representative thereof charged with administering the issuance and/or revocation of permits and licenses under this chapter. 
Livestock means bovine (cows), caprine (goats), equine (horses), ovine (sheep), porcine (pigs), ratite (ostrich) and llamas. 
Llama means a South American camelid which is an animal of the genus lama, commonly referred to as a "one llama," including llamas, alpacas, guanacos, and vicunas. 
Local government means the county board of commissioners. 
Neutered means rendered permanently incapable of reproduction. 
Nuisance means a dog or cat that: 
(1)  Soils or defecates on public roads, walks or recreation areas, or on private property other than the owner's, unless such waste is immediaty removed and properly disposed of by the owner; 
(2)  Causes a disturbance by excessively loud and disturbing noise; or 
(3)  Chases vehicles or molests, attacks or interferes with persons or other domestic animals on public or private property or otherwise causes any damage to any property, private or public. 
Owner means any natural person or any legal entity, including, but not limited to, a corporation, a partnership, firm, or trust owning, possessing, keeping or having custody or control of any domesticated animal within the county. 
Person means any person, firm, corporation, entity, partnership, society or association. 
Potentially dangerous animal means any animal that without provocation bites a human being or other animal, but does not inflict a severe injury. 
Poultry means domestic fowl including, but not limited to, water fowl such as geese and ducks, and birds which are bred for meat and egg production, exhibition, or competition. Such term shall not include ratites, which are considered to be livestock. 
Proper animal health care means a program of disease control and prevention, veterinary care and, when necessary, humane euthanasia. 
Proper enclosure means an enclosure for keeping a dangerous animal or potentially dangerous animal securely confined indoors or in a securely enclosed and locked pen, fence or structure suitable to prevent the entry of young children and which prevents the animal from escaping. Any such pen or structure shall have secure sides and a secure top, and, if the animal is enclosed within a fence, all sides of the fence shall be of sufficient height, and the bottom of the fence shall be constructed or secured in such a manner, as to prevent the animal's escape either from over or under the fence. Any such enclosure shall also provide protection from the elements for the animal. 
Proper enclosure (exotic animal) means a structure constructed, based on requirements of the animal's size, species and breed, to provide sufficient strength to contain the animal securely in all directions and restrict the entrance of unwanted animals and people, protect the animals from injury or suffering, with sufficient space for each animal to turn about freely and to easily move about. Standards used or recognized by federal or state laboratories, universities or accredited zoos shall be utilized by the county to determine the suitability of the structure. 
Qualified dog pound means any dog pound operated by the local government or by an entity with whom the local government has a written agreement regarding the boarding of dogs. 
Records of an appropriate authority means records of any state, county or municipal law enforcement agency; records of any county board of health; records of any federal, state, or local court; or records of an animal control officer or animal control board as provided in this section and by the laws of the state. 
Service of notice means a notice that will be made by official representatives of the county animal control pertaining to any activity governed by this document, and shall include one of the following: 
(1)  Delivery in person of verbal information and/or written documents; 
(2)  Delivery by mail, regular or certified; 
(3)  Delivery by notice of written documents posted in a conspicuous place; or 
(4)  Delivery of information by phone. 
Severe injury means any physical injury that results in broken bones or disfiguring lacerations requiring multiple sutures or cosmetic surgery, or physical injury that results in hospital treatment or death. 
Veterinarian means any person who holds a license to practice veterinary medicine in the state. 
Wild animal means any animal which is not wildlife and is not normally a domesticated animal in this state. This term specifically includes any hybrid or cross between any combination of a wild animal, wildlife, and a domesticated animal. Offspring from all subsequent generations of such crosses or hybrids are wild animals. 
Wildlife means any vertebrate or invertebrate animal life indigenous to this state or any species introduced or specified by the state and includes fish, mammals, birds, fish, amphibians, reptiles, crustaceans, and mollusks or any part thereof. 
(Code 2000, § 30-102; Ord. of 2-5-2002, § 2(exh. B(30-102)); Ord. of 9-12-2006, § 30-102) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-21. 
Sec. 10-3. - Jurisdiction and exceptions to definitions. 
(a)  The jurisdiction of the local government for the enforcement of this chapter shall be the unincorporated areas of the county. 
(b)  The terms "dangerous animal" and "potentially dangerous animal," as defined in section 10-2, shall not include the following: 
(1)  A dog that inflicts an injury upon a person when the dog is being used by a law enforcement officer to carry out the law enforcement officer's official duties; or 
(2)  An animal that inflicts an injury within the meaning of this chapter if the injury was sustained by a person who, at the time, was committing a willful trespass or other tort, or was tormenting, abusing or assaulting the animal, or had in the past been observed or reported to have tormented, abused, or assaulted the animal, or was committing or attempting to commit a crime. 
(c)  Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit the lawful use of any animal in the preparation for and/or the conducting of hunting. 
(d)  No section of this chapter shall apply to livestock, poultry or any animal raised solely for human consumption, unless it is an exotic animal. 
(e)  The animal control officer is authorized to impound animals related to violations of this chapter. 
(f)  The animal control officer is authorized to issue citations for violations of this chapter. 
(Code 2000, § 30-103; Ord. of 2-5-2002, § 2(exh. B(30-103)); Ord. of 9-12-2006, § 30-103) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-21. 
Sec. 10-4. - Hearings. 
(a)  The hearings provided for in section 10-13 shall be held by the county board of commissioners. 
(b)  Any person shall furnish his or her name, address and telephone number when for any reason contacting the county board of commissioners, the animal control officer or any employee of the local government or of a constitutional officer of the county regarding any matter governed under this chapter. 
(Code 2000, § 30-104; Ord. of 2-5-2002, § 2(exh. B(30-104)); Ord. of 9-12-2006, § 30-104) 
State Law reference— County authorized to create animal control board and empower it to hear and determine matters regarding dangerous dogs and potentially dangerous dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-22. 
Sec. 10-5. - Animal control officer appointment. 
The county may appoint an animal control officer. The animal control officer shall serve at the pleasure of the county. The animal control officer shall have the power to issue citations for violations of this chapter. The animal control officer's compensation shall be established from time to time by the county. At the discretion of the county, the animal control officer position may be an additional job given to an existing employee of the county or an employee of a constitutional officer of the county. 
(Code 2000, § 30-105; Ord. of 2-5-2002, § 2(exh. B(30-105)); Ord. of 9-12-2006, § 30-105) 
Sec. 10-6. - Rabies inoculation required. 
(a)  When appropriate for the species, all animals over four months of age within the county must be inoculated for rabies by a state-licensed veterinarian. 
(b)  A certificate of inoculation for rabies shall be issued to the owner of each animal vaccinated, along with an inoculation tag indicating the year issued. The owner must, upon request, provide to the animal control officer a copy of the rabies certificate. 
(c)  The rabies tag shall be secured to a collar on the animal in a manner that it cannot be easily removed or lost by the animal. 
(d)  Any person convicted for a violation of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 2000, § 30-106; Ord. of 2-5-2002, § 2(exh. B(30-106)); Ord. of 9-12-2006, § 30-106) 
State Law reference— County governing authority is responsible for and has power to control rabies through the regulation, licensing, and required inoculation of animals within jurisdiction, O.C.G.A. § 31-19-1 et seq. 
Sec. 10-7. - Animal care; noise; nuisance; feral dogs; cruelty; humane care; dead animal disposal. 
(a)  No person shall permit any dogfight, cockfight, bullfight, or any other combat between animals or between animals and humans. 
(b)  No owner of an animal shall abandon any animal or dead animal. 
(c)  An owner of any animal or fowl who no longer has the means or will to properly care for said animal may voluntarily surrender the animal to the county. To be valid, the surrender of an animal must be accompanied by the written certification and statement of surrender form as provided by the county. Upon the completion of this surrender form, the animal described shall become the property of the county and may be humanely disposed of immediately at the discretion of the animal control officer. 
(d)  No dog owner in the county shall permit same to emit any excessively loud and disturbing noise. 
(e)  Any feral animal may be captured and may immediately become the property of the county. The feral animal may be humanely disposed of immediately at the discretion of the animal control officer. If the feral animal cannot reasonably and/or safely be captured, then reasonable means may be used to ensure the public safety, including but not limited to immediate destruction of the animal. The animal control officer shall have discretion in determining whether an animal is a feral animal or is a domesticated animal with an owner. 
(f)  No animal may be permitted to be a nuisance. 
(g)  It shall be unlawful for any person to work an animal who is lame, starved or in a famished condition, or to overload, whip, beat, maim, bruise, deprive of food, torture or abuse, in any manner, any animal. 
(h)  It shall be unlawful for any person to cause pain, suffering, or death of any living animal, either by an overt act or by any omission or neglect. 
(i)  It shall be unlawful for an owner of an animal to fail to provide that animal with humane care. 
(j)  It shall be unlawful for any person within the county who owns or is caring for an animal that has died or has been killed to abandon the animal, its parts, or blood.
