State Law reference— County authority to remove and dispose of any discarded, dismantled, wrecked, or junked motor vehicles or parts when such are in a condition that constitute a health hazard or unsightly nuisance, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-4. 

Sec. 46-65. - Abandoned, wrecked, etc., motor vehicles declared a public nuisance. 
The presence of any abandoned, wrecked, dismantled, inoperative, rusted, junked, or partially dismantled vehicle or parts thereof, on private or public property is hereby declared a public nuisance which may be abated as such in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(11)) 
Sec. 46-66. - Abandonment prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to abandon, park, store, leave, or permit the parking, storing, or leaving of any motor vehicle of any kind which is in a wrecked, dismantled, inoperative, rusted, junked, or partially dismantled condition whether attended or not, upon any public right-of-way or public property without express permission from the board of commissioners, or on private property without permission from the owner of said property. A vehicle shall be considered abandoned if it remains in one place for a period exceeding 72 hours. 
(b)  This section shall not apply to any vehicle totally enclosed within a building on private property or to any vehicle held in connection with a business enterprise, lawfully licensed by the county, and properly operated in the appropriate business zone, pursuant to the zoning laws of the county, or to any motor vehicle in operable condition specifically adopted or designed for operation on drag strips or raceways, or any vehicle retained by the owner for antique collection purposes. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(11); Ord. of 9-10-2002, § 34-114) 
Sec. 46-67. - Notification; request for hearing; removal of nuisance vehicle. 
(a)  Whenever it comes to the attention of the planning and development office that any motor vehicle declared a public nuisance exists in the county, a notice in writing shall be served upon the occupant of the land where the nuisance vehicle exists, or in case there is no such occupant, then upon the owner of the property or his or her agent, notifying him or her of the existence of the nuisance vehicle and requesting its removal within ten days of such notification. 
(b)  Upon proper notice and opportunity to be heard, the owner of the motor vehicle declared to be a nuisance and the owner and occupant of the private property on which the same is located, either or all of them shall be responsible for its removal. In the event of removal and disposition by the county, the owner or occupant of the private property where the same is located shall be liable for the expenses incurred. 
(c)  Any sworn officer of the court, including but not limited to the sheriff, a sheriff's deputy, the code enforcement officer, building inspector, or assistant building inspector, shall give notice of removal to the owner or occupant of the private property where it is located, at least ten days before the time of compliance. It shall constitute sufficient notice when a copy of the same is posted in a conspicuous place upon the private property on which the nuisance vehicle is located and duplicate copies are sent by registered mail to the owner or occupant of the private property at his or her last known address. 
(d)  The notice shall contain the request for removal within the time specified in this article, and the notice shall advise the owner that, upon failure to comply with the notice to remove, the county or its designee shall undertake such removal with the cost of removal to be levied against the owner or occupant of the property. 
(e)  The persons to whom the notices are directed, or their duly authorized agents, may file a written request for hearing before the board of commissioners, or its designee within the ten-day period of compliance. 
(f)  The hearing shall be held as soon as practicable after the filing of the request and the persons to whom the notices are directed shall be advised of the time and place of said hearing at least five days in advance thereof. At any such hearing, the county and the persons to whom the notices have been directed may introduce such witnesses and evidence as either party deems necessary. 
(g)  If the violation described in the notice has not been remedied within the ten-day period of compliance, or in the event that a notice requesting the hearing is timely filed and a hearing is held, and the existence of the violation is affirmed by the board of commissioners, the sheriff, or his or her designee, shall have the right to take possession of the motor vehicle declared a nuisance and remove it from the premises. It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere with, hinder, or refuse to allow such person or persons to enter upon private property for the purpose of removing a vehicle under the provisions of this article. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(15)) 
Sec. 46-68. - Sale of removed motor vehicle. 
(a)  Within 48 hours of the removal of any motor vehicle removed pursuant to this article, the sheriff, or his or her designee, shall give notice to the registered owner of the vehicle, if known, and also to the owner or occupant of the private property from which the vehicle was removed, that said vehicle has been impounded and stored for violation of this article. The notice shall give the location of where the vehicle is stored, and the costs incurred by the county for removal. 
(b)  Upon removing a vehicle under the provisions of this article, the sheriff, or his or her designee, shall proceed to have the property sold in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 9-13-140 et seq. 
(c)  The notice of the sale shall state: 
(1)  The sale is of abandoned property in the possession of the county; 
(2)  A description of the vehicle, including make, model, license number and any other information which will accurately identify that vehicle; 
(3)  The terms of the sale; 
(4)  The date, time, and place of the sale; and 
(5)  Any other information required by state law. 
(d)  The vehicle shall be sold to the highest and best bidder. At the time of payment of the purchase price, the sheriff shall execute a certificate of sale in duplicate, the original of which to be given to the purchaser, and the copy thereof to be filed with the tax commissioner. Should the sale for any reason be invalid, the county's liability shall be limited to the return of the purchase price. A credit shall be given to the property owner for any net monies received from any sale of said property by the board of commissioners. 
(e)  The owner of any vehicle seized under the provisions of this article may redeem such vehicle at any time after its removal but prior to the sale or destruction thereof upon proof of ownership and payment to the county of said sum as it may determine and fix for the actual reasonable expense or removal, and any preliminary sale advertising expenses, all of said sums not to exceed $500.00 plus $10.00 per day storage for each vehicle redeemed. 
(f)  Upon the failure of the owner or occupant of property on which abandoned vehicles have been removed by the county to pay the unrecovered expenses by the county in such removal, a lien shall be placed upon the property for the amount of such expenses. 
(g)  Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and subject to the general penalties described in section 1-9. Each day such violation is committed or permitted to continue shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(15)) 
Secs. 46-69—46-89. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - OUTDOOR STORAGE 

Sec. 46-90. - Enclosure required; exemption. 
(a)  Inventory items and manufacturing scrap materials and byproducts at all business and industrial locations shall be stored inside a fenced enclosure at the rear or to the side of the facility. Fencing shall be six feet in height and shall be constructed of materials which provide a nonvisible screen. Retail items and manufacturing products offered for sale to the general public or retailers are excluded from this subsection. 
(b)  Old appliances, scrap materials, building materials, parts to machinery and similar type items which are not legitimate inventory items must be stored inside an enclosed building. Such items must be stored in such a manner so as not to be visible to surrounding properties. Retail items and manufacturing products offered for sale to the general public or retailers are excluded from this subsection. 
(c)  Any of the items noted in subsections (a) and (b) of this section found to be stored other than as provided for in this section are hereby declared a public nuisance which may be abated as such in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. Buildings or additions to buildings which are under construction with a valid building permit will be exempt from this requirement. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(12)) 
Secs. 46-91—46-114. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - UNFIT BUILDINGS OR STRUCTURES 

Sec. 46-115. - Purpose and authority. 
This article is adopted pursuant to the authority granted by O.C.G.A. title 41, ch. 2, for the purpose of maintaining the health and cleanliness of the county, and to ensure safe and sanitary conditions in private premises in the county by establishing a method for enforcing minimum housing standards within the jurisdiction of the county. The provisions of this article are hereby declared to be necessary for reasons of the public health, safety and welfare. The county recognizes that dwellings, buildings, structures or conditions exist within the county that are unfit for human habitation or commercial, industrial or business uses. 
(Code 2000, § 35-101) 
Sec. 46-116. - Findings and applicability. 
(a)  It is found and declared that there exist in the county dwellings, buildings or structures which are unfit for human habitation or for commercial, industrial or business uses due to dilapidation and defects increasing the hazards of fire, accidents or other calamities, infestation, lack of adequate ventilation, light, or sanitary facilities; or other conditions rendering such dwellings, buildings, or structures unsafe or unsanitary or dangerous or detrimental to the health, safety or welfare, or otherwise inimical to the welfare of the residents of this county, and that this county should exercise its police power to provide for the repair, closing or demolition of the aforesaid dwellings, buildings or structures in the manner provided in this article. 
(b)  All the provisions of this article, including methods and procedures, may also be applied to private property where an accumulation of weeds, trash, junk, filth, or other unsanitary or unsafe conditions shall create an actual or potential public health hazard or general nuisance to those persons residing in the vicinity. A finding by any governmental department, officer or inspector that such property is a health or safety hazard shall constitute prima facie evidence that such property is in violation of this article. 
(Code 2000, § 35-103) 
Sec. 46-117. - Unlawful to own, sell, rent or lease; definition of vacancy. 
It shall be unlawful and a misdemeanor for any owner, whether directly or through an agent, to own, sell, rent or lease to any person any unfit structure for the purpose of living, sleeping, cooking, eating, usage or occupancy of any kind, when said owner has been notified in accordance with this article that such structure is an unfit structure. This shall apply to any deteriorated structure, even if vacant. 
(Code 2000, § 35-104) 
Sec. 46-118. - Abatement procedures. 
(a)  Whenever a request is filed with the director of planning and development by a public authority, or by a written complaint filed by anyone, charging that any dwelling, building or structure is unfit for human habitation or for commercial, industrial or business use, or whenever it appears to the director of planning and development (on his or her own motion) that any dwelling, building or structure is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial or business use, the director of planning and development shall, if his or her preliminary investigation discloses a basis for such charges, issue and cause to be served upon the owner of and any parties in interest in such dwelling, building, or structure a complaint stating the charges in that respect and containing a notice that a hearing will be held before the director of planning and development at a place within the county, fixed not less than ten days or more than 30 days after the serving of the complaint. The owner and any parties in interest shall be given the right to file an answer to the complaint and to appear in person, or otherwise, and give testimony at the place and time fixed in the complaint, and the rules of evidence prevailing in courts of law or equity shall not be controlling in hearings before the director of planning and development. 
(b)  If, after such notice and hearing, the director of planning and development determines that the dwelling, building, or structure under consideration is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial or business use, he or she shall state in writing the findings of fact in support of such determination and shall issue and cause to be served upon the owner thereof an order: 
(1)  If the repair, alteration, or improvement of such dwelling, building or structure can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, building or structure, requiring the owner or parties in interest, within the time specified in the order, to repair, alter or improve such dwelling, building or structure so as to render it fit for human habitation or for current commercial, industrial or business use or to vacate and close the dwelling, building or structure for human habitation; or 
(2)  If the repair, alteration, or improvement of such dwelling, building or structure cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, building or structure, requiring the owner or parties in interest within the time specified in the order, to remove or demolish such dwelling, building or structure. 
(c)  Any party in interest who takes exception to said order may seek an injunction against the enforcement of the order by presenting a petition therefor to the superior court within 15 days of service of the order, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 41-2-13. In no event shall the director of planning and development require removal or demolition of any dwelling, building, or structure except upon a finding that the cost of repair, alteration or improvement thereof exceeds one-half the value of such dwelling, building or structure when repaired to satisfy the minimum requirements of this article. 
(d)  If the owner or parties in interest fail to comply with an order to vacate and close or demolish the dwelling, building or structure, and do not seek an injunction under O.C.G.A. § 41-2-13, the director of planning and development may cause such dwelling, building or structure to be repaired, altered or improved or to be vacated and closed or demolished; and the director of planning and development may cause to be posted on the main entrance of any building, dwelling or structure so closed a placard with the following words: 
"This building is unfit for human habitation or commercial, industrial, or business use; the use or occupation of this building for human habitation or for commercial, industrial or business use is prohibited and unlawful." 
(e)  If the owner fails to comply with any order to remove or demolish the dwelling, building or structure, the director of planning and development may cause such dwelling, building or structure to be removed or demolished. 
(f)  The amount of the cost of such vacating and closing or removal or demolition by the director of planning and development shall be a lien against the real property upon which cost was incurred. Such lien shall attach to the real property upon the payment of all costs of demolition by the county and the filing of an itemized statement of the total sum of such costs by the director of planning and development in the office of the county clerk on a lien docket maintained by such clerk for such purposes. If the dwelling, building or structure is removed or demolished by the director of planning and development, he or she shall sell any valuable materials of such dwellings, buildings or structures and shall credit the proceeds of such sale against the cost of the removal or demolition, and any balance remaining shall be deposited in the superior court by the director of planning and development, shall be secured in such manner as may be directed by such court, and shall be disbursed by such court to the persons found to be entitled thereto by final order or decree of such court. Nothing in this section shall be construed to impair or limit in any way the power of the county to define and declare nuisances and to cause their removal or abatement by summary proceedings or otherwise. 
(g)  The county may enforce the collection of any amount due on such lien for removal or demolition of dwellings, buildings or structures only in the following manner: 
(1)  The owner or parties in interest shall be allowed to satisfy the amount due on such lien by paying to the county within 30 days after the perfection of such lien, a sum of money equal to 25 percent of the total amount due and by further paying to the county the remaining balance due on such lien, together with interest at the rate of seven percent per annum, in three equal annual payments, each of which shall become due and payable on the anniversary date of the initial payment made as prescribed in this subsection (g)(1). 
(2)  Should the property upon which such lien is perfected be sold, transferred or conveyed by the owner or parties in interest at any time prior to the termination of the three-year period, then the entire balance due on such lien shall be due and payable to the county at the time of the sale, transfer or conveyance; and 
(3)  Should such lien, or any portion thereof, be unpaid after the passage of said three-year period, or upon the occurrence of the contingency provided for in subsection (g)(2) of this section, the county may enforce the collection of any amount due on such lien for alteration, repair, removal or demolition of dwellings, buildings, or structures in the same manner as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-5-358, and other applicable state statutes. This procedure shall be subject to the right of redemption by any persons having any right, title or interest in or lien upon such property, all as provided by O.C.G.A. § 48-4-40 et seq. 
(Code 2000, § 35-105) 
Sec. 46-119. - Determination of unfitness. 
The director of planning and development may determine that a dwelling, building or structure is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial or business use if he or she finds that conditions exist in such building, dwelling or structure which are dangerous or injurious to the health, safety or morals of the occupants of such dwelling, building or structure; of the occupants of neighborhood dwellings, buildings or structures; or of other residents of the county; such conditions may include, without limiting the generality of the preceding conditions, the following: 
(1)  Defects therein increasing the hazards of fire, accidents, or other calamities; 
(2)  Lack of adequate ventilation, light or sanitary facilities; 
(3)  Dilapidation; 
(4)  Disrepair; 
(5)  Structural defects; 
(6)  Uncleanliness; 
(7)  The interior walls or other vertical structural members list, lean or buckle so that a plumb line passing through the center of gravity of the structural members falls outside of its base so as to create a hazardous condition to the occupants of the structure or the population of the surrounding area; 
(8)  Due to their unsafe condition, the supporting structure and/or nonsupporting enclosing or outside walls must be replaced; 
(9)  The floors or roofs have improperly distributed loads or oversized loads, or are so weakened as to be unsafe for their present or intended use; 
(10)  The structure has been damaged by wind, fire or other causes so as to imperil the safety or the health of the structure's occupants or of the people of the county; 
(11)  Conditions which may be detrimental to the public health, safety and/or welfare whether found in a structure or on the premises surrounding the structure, including but not limited to abandoned wells, shafts, basements or excavations, abandoned refrigerators and motor vehicles, or any structurally unsound fences or any lumber, trash, fences, debris or vegetation, or any condition which may cause lack of safe ingress or egress to the structure; 
(12)  The premises are vacant, dilapidated and being used in connection with drug crimes. 
(Code 2000, § 35-106) 
Sec. 46-120. - Powers of public officers. 
The public officer shall exercise such powers as may be necessary or convenient to carry out and effectuate the purpose and provisions of this article, including, among others granted herein, the power to: 
(1)  Investigate the dwelling conditions in the county in order to determine which dwellings, buildings or structures therein are unfit for human habitation or are unfit for current commercial, industrial, or business use, or are vacant, dilapidated and being used in connection with the commission of drug crimes; 
(2)  Administer oaths and affirmations, examine witnesses, and receive evidence; 
(3)  Enter upon premises for the purpose of making examinations; provided, however, that such entries shall be made in such manner as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the persons in possession; 
(4)  Appoint and fix the duties of such officers, agents, and employees as he or she deems necessary to carry out the purposes of this article; and 
(5)  Delegate any of his or her functions and powers under this article to such officers and agents as he or she may designate. 
(Code 2000, § 35-107) 
Sec. 46-121. - Service of complaints or orders. 
(a)  Complaints or orders issued by a public officer pursuant to this article shall, in all cases, be served upon each person in possession of such property, each owner and each party in interest; and the return of service signed by the public officer or an affidavit of service executed by any adult citizen of this state, reciting that a copy of such complaint or orders was served upon each person in possession of such property, each owner, and each party in interest personally, or by leaving such copy at the place of his or her residence, shall be sufficient evidence as to the service of such person in possession, owner and party in interest. 
(b)  If any of the owners and parties in interest shall reside outside of the county, service shall be perfected by causing a copy of such complaint or orders to be served upon such party or parties, by the sheriff or any lawful deputy of the county of residence of such party, or such service may be made by any adult citizen; and the return of such sheriff or lawful deputy or the affidavit of such adult citizen, that such party or parties were served either personally or by leaving a copy of the complaint or orders at such party's residence, shall be conclusive as to such service. 
(c)  Nonresidents of this state shall be served by publishing the complaint or orders for two successive weeks in the legal organ of the county, and by posting a copy of such complaint or orders in a conspicuous place on the premises affected by the complaint or orders. Where the address of such nonresidents is known, a copy of such complaint or orders shall be mailed to them by registered or certified mail. 
(d)  In the event either the owner or any party in interest is a minor or an insane person or a person laboring under disabilities, the guardian or other personal representative of such person shall be served, and if such guardian or personal representative resides outside the county or is a nonresident, he or she shall be served as provided in this section in such cases. If such minor or insane person or person laboring under disabilities has no guardian or personal representative or in the event such minor or insane person lives outside the county or is a nonresident, service shall be perfected by serving such minor or insane person personally or by leaving a copy at such minor's or insane person's place of residence which shall be sufficient evidence as to the service of such person or persons; in the case of other persons who live outside of the county or are nonresidents, service shall be perfected by serving the judge of the probate court of the county, who shall stand in the place of and protect the rights of such minor or insane persons or appoint a guardian ad litem for such person. 
(e)  In the event the whereabouts of any owner or party in interest is unknown and the same cannot be ascertained by the public officer in the exercise of reasonable diligence, the public officer shall make an affidavit to that effect, and the service of such complaint or orders upon such person shall be made in the same manner as provided in subsection (c) of this section, and service may be further perfected upon any person, firm or corporation holding itself out as an agent for the property involved. 
(f)  A copy of such complaint or orders shall also be filed in the proper office or offices for the filing of lis pendens notice in the county, and such filing of the complaint or orders shall have the same force and effect as other lis pendens notices provided by law. Any such complaint or orders or an appropriate lis pendens notice may contain a statement to the effect that a lien may arise against the described property and that an itemized statement of such lien is maintained on a lien docket maintained by the county. 
(Code 2000, § 35-108) 
Sec. 46-122. - Use of revenues, grants and donations to repair, close or demolish. 
The county may make such appropriations from its revenues as it may deem necessary and may accept and apply grants or donations to assist it in carrying out the provisions of this article. 
(Code 2000, § 35-109) 
Sec. 46-123. - Deteriorated structures and premises as nuisances. 
(a)  All structures and/or the surrounding premises of the structures which are determined to be in violation of this article are hereby declared to be public nuisances. In those instances where there is an imminent threat to life or safety, the public officer shall be authorized to immediately post the structure as unsafe for human habitation. 
(b)  If such finding of the public officer is contested by the occupants of the structure, then the public officer shall request an immediate hearing before the judge of the magistrate court in order to secure an order requiring any occupants of the unsafe structures to vacate. The public officer shall then proceed as set forth in this article. 
(Code 2000, § 35-110) 
Sec. 46-124. - Conflict of laws. 
Nothing in this article shall be construed to abrogate or impair the powers of the courts or of any department of the county to enforce any provisions of the Charter or the local ordinances or regulations, nor to prevent or punish violations thereof. The powers conferred by this article shall be in addition to and supplemental to the powers conferred by any other law or ordinance. 
(Code 2000, § 35-111) 
ARTICLE VI. - FORECLOSURE REGISTRY[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2012-002, § 1(exh. A), adopted Sept. 4, 2012, amended Art. VI in its entirety to read as herein set out. Former Art. VI, §§ 46-125—46-129, pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Ord. of 4-5-2011, §§ 1—3(exh. A). 

Sec. 46-125. - Purpose. 
Neighborhoods are facing significant threat of becoming blighted through the lack of adequate maintenance and security of properties that are abandoned, foreclosed or where ownership has been transferred after foreclosure. Improperly maintained and secured abandoned and/or foreclosed properties can become a hazard to the health and safety of persons who may come on or near the property and can adversely affect the aesthetic and economic attributes of communities. Difficulties also often arise in locating the person responsible for the condition of abandoned and/or foreclosed real property. There is a substantial need directly related to the public health, safety and welfare to comprehensively address these concerns through the adoption of the provisions in this article. 
This foreclosure registry will require creditors or mortgagees to provide the county with official information for contacting a party responsible for bringing abandoned and/or foreclosed real property into compliance with applicable provisions of Chapter 14—Buildings and Building Regulations, Chapter 42—Natural Resources, Chapter 46—Nuisances and Chapter 58—Solid Waste of the Code of Morgan County, Georgia. 
(Ord. No. 2012-002, § 1(exh. A), 9-4-2012) 
Sec. 46-126. - Definitions. 
In addition to the definitions contained in sections 1-2 and 46-1, the following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Agent means an individual with a place of business in this state at which he or she is authorized to accept inquiries, notices on behalf of a vacant or foreclosed real property owner. Such agent must be authorized and empowered by the foreclosed real property owner to: 
(1)  To ensure security and maintenance; 
(2)  To comply with code enforcement orders issued by the county; 
(3)  To provide a trespass authorization upon request of an enforcement officer; 
(4)  To conduct inspections; 
(5)  To accept rental payments from tenants, if no management company is otherwise employed; and 
(6)  To serve as an agent authorized to receive any citation under this chapter and notice pertaining to any court proceeding or administrative enforcement proceeding in connection with the enforcement of this chapter, including service of process. 
Abandoned means real property that is vacant and is under a notice of default and/or notice of trustee's sale, pending tax commissioner lien sale and/or properties that have been subject of a previous foreclosure sale in which title was retained by the beneficiary of a deed of trust involved in the foreclosure and any properties transferred under a deed in lieu of foreclosure and/or sale. 
County means Morgan County, Georgia. 
Creditor means a person or entity to whom a debt is owed or who has a right to require the fulfillment of an obligation or contract, wherein said debt or right is secured by a deed to secure debt, deed of trust or other instrument conveying a lien upon or security in title to real property. 
Days means consecutive calendar days. 
Enforcement officer means any law enforcement officer, building official, fire inspector or code enforcement officer employed by or working on behalf of the county. 
Foreclosed real property means improved or unimproved real property for which a land disturbance permit has been issued and is held pursuant to a judicial or nonjudicial foreclosure of a mortgage, deed of trust, security deed, deed to secure debt, or other security instrument securing a debt or obligation owed to a creditor or a deed in lieu of foreclosure in full or partial satisfaction of a debt or obligation owed to a creditor. 
Form means the foreclosed or vacant property registration form created by the Georgia Department of Community Affairs registry. 
Real property means any improved or unimproved residential or commercial land or portion thereof identified by a map and parcel identification number, located in the unincorporated areas of the county. 
Registry official means the county's chief building inspector/director of planning and development. 
Street address means the street or route address. Such term shall not mean or include a post office box. 
Transferree means the person or entity to whom foreclosed real property is first transferred by a creditor after foreclosure. 
Vacant real property means real property that: 
(1)  Is intended for habitation, has not been lawfully inhabited for at least 60 days, and has no evidence of utility usage within the past 60 days; or 
(2)  Is partially constructed or incomplete, without a valid building permit. 
Such term shall not include a building or structure containing multiple units with common ownership that has at least one unit occupied with evidence of utility usage. 
(Ord. No. 2012-002, § 1(exh. A), 9-4-2012) 
Sec. 46-127. - Registry of foreclosed real property. 
Any creditor who obtains foreclosed real property by way of a foreclosure sale or proceeding shall, within 91 days of obtaining such property, pay to the county a registration fee for each foreclosed real property in accordance with the fee schedules set by the board of commissioners, not to exceed $100.00 per foreclosed real property, and register with the county by completing and turning in the form, providing the following information: 
(1)  Creditor's name, street address, mailing address, telephone number, facsimile number, and e-mail address; 
(2)  Agent's name, street address, mailing address, telephone number, facsimile number, and e-mail address; 
(3)  The street address, including tax map and parcel identification number, of the foreclosed real property; 
(4)  The date on which the property was transferred, as stated on the instrument conveying the real property, whether that instrument has been recorded or not; and 
(5)  At such time as it becomes available, recording information, including deed book and page numbers, of the instrument conveying the real property to the owner. 
(Ord. No. 2012-002, § 1(exh. A), 9-4-2012) 
Sec. 46-128. - Registry of transferred foreclosed real property. 
Any creditor who has foreclosed on real property and then transfers said foreclosed real property to another person or entity shall, within 91 days of said transfer, pay to the county a registration fee for each transferred foreclosed real property in accordance with the fee schedules set by the board of commissioners, not to exceed $100.00, and register with the county at that time, by completing and turning in the form, providing the following information: 
(1)  Transferee's name, street address, mailing address, telephone number, facsimilie number, and e-mail address; 
(2)  Agent's name, street address, mailing address, telephone number, facsimile number, and e-mail address; 
(3)  The street address, including tax map and parcel identification number, of the foreclosed real property; 
(4)  The date on which the property was transferred, as stated on the instrument conveying the real property, whether that instrument has been recorded or not; and 
(5)  At such time as it becomes available, recording information, including deed book and page numbers, of the instrument conveying the real property to the owner. 
(Ord. No. 2012-002, § 1(exh. A), 9-4-2012) 
Sec. 46-129. - Exemption from registration requirements. 
No creditor or other owner of foreclosed real property shall be required to register such foreclosed real property under sections 46-127 or 46-128, nor shall such creditor or owner be required to pay any registration fee, if: 
(1)  The deed under power of sale or deed in lieu of foreclosure under which the creditor or owner takes the property contains the information specified in paragraphs (1) through (5) of sections 46-127 or 46-128; 
(2)  The deed is filed with the clerk of superior court within 60 days of the transfer; and 
(3)  Proof of the following is provided to the office or officer in charge of the county foreclosed real property registry: 
a.  A filing date stamp or a receipt showing payment of the applicable filing fees; and 
b.  A recorded copy of the entire deed under power of sale or entire deed in lieu of foreclosure. 
(Ord. No. 2012-002, § 1(exh. A), 9-4-2012) 
Sec. 46-130. - Removal from registry. 
A vacant or foreclosed real property owner, or the agent of such owner, may apply to remove such vacant or foreclosed real property from the registry at such time as the real property no longer constitutes vacant or foreclosed real property. Such application shall be made on forms provided by the county, and shall include the following: 
(1)  The reason the property is no longer vacant or foreclosed real property; 
(2)  The current owner's name, street address, mailing address, telephone number, facsimilie number, and e-mail address; 
(3)  The street address, including tax map and parcel identification number, of the foreclosed real property; 
(4)  The date on which the property was no longer vacant or foreclosed real property; and 
(5)  If the reason for removal is the transfer of the property to a new owner who has inhabited the property or is actively engaged in improving the property pursuant to a valid building permit, then at such time as it becomes available, provide the recording information, including deed book and page numbers, of the instrument conveying the real property to the new owner. 
The registry official shall grant or deny such application within 30 days of receipt of a fully completed application, and if no such determination is made within 30 days, the application shall be deemed granted. 
(Ord. No. 2012-002, § 1(exh. A), 9-4-2012) 
Sec. 46-131. - Administration, enforcement, appeals, violations and penalties. 
(a)  All creditors and transferees subject to registration or registered pursuant to this article shall: 
(1)  Comply with applicable provisions of this chapter; 
(2)  Utilize the form as required; and 
(3)  Report any change in the required information set forth in sections 46-128(1)—(5) and 46-129 to the county within 30 days of the change, regardless of whether such information was in the deed under power of sale or deed in lieu of foreclosure. 
(b)  County may make foreclosure registry information accessible online. 
(c)  Registration information shall be deemed prima facie proof of the statements contained therein in any court proceeding or administrative enforcement proceeding in connection with the enforcement of this chapter. 
(d)  Registry official is in charge of administering the provisions of this article, and as such has the sole authority and discretion to determine compliance, to grant or deny applications for removal from the registry, and to determine whether a creditor, transferee or owner is required to register property pursuant to this article. Nothing contained in this subsection shall be construed to prohibit or limit the ability of other enforcement officers from issuing citations for violations of this article. 
(e)  Any person aggrieved of a decision by the registry official may appeal that decision to the Magistrate Court of Morgan County within 30 days of: 
(1)  The issuance of a citation for violating this article; or 
(2)  The date of the written decision denying the application or request. The person aggrieved shall have three additional days added to the 30 days if the written decision is mailed, rather than hand-delivered. 
(f)  Violation of this article shall be treated as a strict liability offense regardless of intent and shall be punishable by a fine not to exceed $1,000.00 per violation. 
(Ord. No. 2012-002, § 1(exh. A), 9-4-2012) 
Secs. 46-132—46-144. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - ENFORCEMENT[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note— This article was formerly numbered as Article VI, and was renumbered by Ord. of 4-5-2011, § 1. 

Sec. 46-145. - Responsibility; right of entry; power of summons. 
Enforcement of this chapter shall be the responsibility of any sworn officer of the court, including, but not limited to, the sheriff, deputy sheriff, the code enforcement officer, building inspector, or assistant building inspector. Any person or persons authorized to enforce this chapter shall be empowered to enter any property, upon reasonable cause, at reasonable times in order to inspect the property for violations of this chapter, subject to the conditions that to allow entry on private property for inspection, the alleged violation of this chapter must be visible from a public road or right-of-way, or upon such officer having received a written complaint alleging a violation of this chapter. The magistrate court shall also be authorized to issue summons for hearings on alleged violations of this chapter upon written accusation of any person sui juris alleging such violation. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(16)) 
Sec. 46-146. - Violations; penalties. 
(a)  Any person, firm, or corporation violating any provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished according to the general penalty described in section 1-9. 
(b)  In addition, in the sound discretion of a court in which conviction is obtained: 
(1)  The violator may be directed to pick up and remove from any public street or highway, or public right-of-way for a distance not to exceed one mile any litter said person has deposited and any and all litter deposited thereon by anyone else prior to the date of the execution of sentence; 
(2)  The violator may be directed to pick up and remove from a public park, private right-of-way, or with the prior permission of the legal owner or tenant in lawful possession of such property, any private property upon which it can be established by competent evidence that the violator has deposited thereon by anyone prior to the date of execution of the sentence; and/or 
(3)  The court may publish the names of offenders convicted of violating this chapter. 
(c)  In the case of an improper garbage or waste disposal site, the property owner, contractor, developer, builder or other person responsible for the property shall cause the property to be cleaned and to come into full compliance with this chapter. 
(d)  The county shall not be responsible for any costs of cleanup or remediation. 
(e)  Each day that a violation of any section under this chapter is committed or permitted to continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable as such. 
(Code 2000, §§ 12-101(17), 33-104) 
State Law reference— Any person who shall erect or continue after notice to abate a nuisance which tends to annoy the community, injure the health of the citizens in general, or corrupt the public morals shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, O.C.G.A. § 41-1-6. 
Sec. 46-147. - Civil remedies; abatement. 
As an additional remedy, any person, firm, or corporation that violates any provision of this chapter causing discomfort or annoyance to reasonable persons of normal sensitiveness or which endangers the comfort, repose, health or peace of residents in the area may be subject to abatement summarily by a restraining order, mandamus, injunction or other appropriate action or proceeding to prevent such unlawful act or to correct or abate such violation. 
(Code 2000, §§ 12-101(7), 33-105) 
Sec. 46-148. - Cleaning property at expense of owner or occupant. 
(a)  Upon the first violation of any provisions of this chapter, the county manager, or a designated county official, shall issue a warning citation to the owner and/or occupant of the offending property, instructing the person cited to remedy the unlawful condition within 30 days from the date of the warning citation. If the person cited fails to so remedy the offending property within that 30-day time period, the county is authorized but not required to clean the offending property to bring it into compliance with the provisions of this chapter. In order to do so, the county through its agents may: 
(1)  Remove any unlawful litter, junk, automobiles, weeds and/or grasses that exist thereon and bill the owner for the cost thereof. If the owner and/or occupant fails or refuses to pay bills for cleanup service within 30 days from the date of billing, then execution may be issued by the county against the property upon which such service is rendered for the amount of the cleanup service charge; and from and after the recording of such execution on the general execution docket in the office of the clerk of the superior court of the county, such execution shall constitute a lien on the property which the service is rendered until the same shall have been fully paid and satisfied. Such executions may be enforced in the same manner and with the addition of interest and costs as provided by law for the enforcement of executions for ad valorem taxes for the county; or 
(2)  Contract with private individuals or entities to clean the offending property by removing the unlawful litter, junk, automobiles, weeds and/or grasses that exist thereon, allowing the private individuals or entities to collect their costs and expenses from either the cited owner and/or occupant directly or through the sale of any junk or scrap removed from the offending property. 
(b)  After an owner and/or occupant of property has been issued a warning citation instructing the person to remedy an unlawful condition under this chapter, and the owner and/or occupant has allowed or caused an unlawful condition to occur on the same property again, the county is authorized but not required to clean the offending property to bring it into compliance with the provisions of this chapter in the manner set forth in subsections (a)(1) and (2) of this section, but the county shall not be required to issue any warning citation, nor will the offending owner or occupant of property be entitled to 30 days to remedy the violation. 
(c)  Action by the county under this section shall not preclude criminal prosecution for a violation of any other section of this chapter, and the remedies authorized in this section are exclusive of any other criminal penalties and fines that may be assessed under this Code. 
(Code 2000, §§ 12-101(10)(b); Ord. of 9-10-2002, § 34-116) 
Chapter 50 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 50-1. - Purchase or consumption of intoxicating beverages by minors prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful within the unincorporated areas of the county for any person under 21 years of age to purchase intoxicating beverages or for any person to consume said intoxicating beverages at any retail malt beverage and/or wine establishment within the unincorporated areas of the county except as otherwise allowed by law. 
(b)  The penalty for a violation of this section shall be as provided in section 1-9. Each day such violation is committed or permitted to continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable as such hereunder. 
(c)  Violations of this section shall be prosecuted in the same manner as other misdemeanor violations of the Code in the magistrate court, or any other appropriate court. 
(Code 2000, § 31-101) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-9. 
Sec. 50-2. - Public intoxication prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person within the unincorporated areas of the county to be and appear in an intoxicated condition in any public place or within the curtilage of any private residence not his or her own other than by invitation of the owner or lawful occupant, which condition is made manifest by boisterousness, by indecent condition or act, or by vulgar, profane, loud, or unbecoming language. 
(b)  The penalty for a violation of this section shall be as provided in section 1-9. Each day such violation is committed or permitted to continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable as such hereunder. 
(c)  Violations of this section shall be prosecuted in the same manner as other misdemeanor violations of the Code. 
(Code 2000, § 31-102) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-41. 
Sec. 50-3. - Loitering regulations. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter within the unincorporated areas of the county. 
(b)  A person commits the offense of loitering or prowling when he or she is in a place at a time or in a manner not usual for law abiding individuals under circumstances that warrant a justifiable and reasonable alarm or immediate concern for the safety of persons or property in the vicinity. 
(c)  Among the circumstances which may be considered in determining whether alarm is warranted is the fact that the person takes flight upon the appearance of a law enforcement officer, refuses to identify himself or herself, or manifestly endeavors to conceal himself or herself or any object. Unless flight by the person or other circumstances make impractical, a law enforcement officer shall, prior to any arrest for an offense under this section, afford the person an opportunity to dispel any alarm or immediate concern which would otherwise be warranted by requesting the person to identify himself or herself and explain his or her presence and conduct. No person shall be convicted of an offense under this section if the law enforcement officer unreasonably failed to comply with the foregoing procedure or if it appears at trial that the explanation given by the person was true and would have dispelled the alarm or immediate concern. 
(d)  The penalty for a violation of this section shall be as provided in section 1-9. Each day such violation is committed or permitted to continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable as such hereunder. 
(e)  Violations of this section shall be prosecuted in the same manner as other misdemeanor violations of the Code in the magistrate court or any other appropriate court. 
(Code 2000, § 31-104) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-36. 
Sec. 50-4. - Damage to signs prohibited. 
(a)  No person shall remove, disfigure, deface, destroy or in any manner interfere with the use of public signs (i.e., a sign owned by a governmental entity). 
(b)  Any person violating this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be subject to a fine of not more than $500.00 per violation of this section. 
(Code 2000, § 31-106) 
Sec. 50-5. - Disorderly conduct. 
(a)  A person shall be guilty of disorderly conduct if, within the unincorporated areas of the county, with the purpose of causing public danger, alarm, disorder, nuisance, or if his or her conduct is likely to cause public danger, alarm, disorder or nuisance, he or she willfully does any of the following acts in a public place: 
(1)  Commits an act in a violent and tumultuous manner toward another whereby that other is placed in danger of his or her life, limb or health; 
(2)  Commits an act in a violent and tumultuous manner toward another where the property of any person is placed in danger of being destroyed or damaged; 
(3)  Causes, provokes or engages in any fight, brawl or riotous conduct so as to endanger the life, limb, health or property of another; 
(4)  If in a public place under the influence of an intoxicating liquor or drug in such condition as to be unable to exercise care for his or her own safety or the safety of others; 
(5)  Uses abusive or obscene language or makes an obscene gesture. 
(b)  This section shall not be construed to suppress the right to lawful assembly, picketing, public speaking, or other lawful means of expressing public opinion not in contravention of other laws. 
(c)  The penalty for a violation of this section shall be as provided in section 1-9. 
(Code 2000, § 31-107) 
State Law reference— County has joint jurisdiction with state regarding this offense, O.C.G.A. §§ 16-11-34, 16-11-39, 16-11-41. 
Sec. 50-6. - Interference with business enterprise of another. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to enter upon the premises of another, located within the unincorporated areas of the county, for the purpose of interfering, either directly or indirectly, with the business of said person or to interfere directly or indirectly with the business of any person. 
(b)  The penalty for a violation of this section shall be as provided in section 1-9. Any such violation shall constitute a separate offense each time committed. Such violations may be prosecuted in the magistrate court or any other appropriate court. 
(Code 2000, § 31-108) 
Sec. 50-7. - Report of treatment of wounds. 
All physicians and all hospital superintendents in the county are hereby required to report to the sheriff's department of the county all patients treated by physicians or diagnosed or known to be suffering from wounds inflicted by a dangerous or deadly weapon of any kind. Such report may be made in writing or by telephone, giving the name of the reporting person and the patient and any other pertinent data requested by the sheriff's department. All reports shall be made within 24 hours after treatment by a physician or after admission to the hospital. 
(Code 2000, § 31-110) 
State Law reference— Reports by physicians and other personnel of nonaccidental injuries to patients, O.C.G.A. § 31-7-9. 
Sec. 50-8. - Throwing of missiles prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person in the county to throw any stone, rock, or other missile upon or at any vehicle, building, tree, or other public or private property, or upon or at any person in any public or private way or place. 
(Code 2000, § 31-111) 
Sec. 50-9. - Open container. 
(a)  As used in this section, "open container" means any container which is immediately capable of being consumed from, or the seal of which has been broken. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful and punishable as provided in this section for any person to possess an open container of any alcoholic beverage (including but not limited to beer, wine or liquor) while operating a vehicle within the unincorporated areas of Morgan County, Georgia, or while a passenger in or on a vehicle being operated within said unincorporated areas. 
(c)  An open container shall be considered to be in the possession of the operator of a vehicle if the container is not in the possession of a passenger and is not located in a locked glove compartment, locked trunk, or other locked non-passenger area of the vehicle. 
(d)  An open container shall be considered to be in the possession of a passenger of a vehicle if the container is in the physical control of the passenger. 
(e)  This section shall not apply to: 
(1)  A passenger of a vehicle in which the driver is operating the vehicle pursuant to a contract to provide transportation for passengers and such driver holds a valid chauffeur's license pursuant to Georgia law or any other state; 
(2)  A passenger of a bus in which the driver holds a valid chauffeur's license pursuant to Georgia law or any other state; or 
(3)  A passenger of a self-contained motor home which is in excess of 21 feet in length. 
(f)  Any person, operator of a vehicle, or passenger who violates this section shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $500.00 or 30 days in jail, or both. 
(Ord. of 12-4-2007(2), § 1) 
Sec. 50-10. - Discharging firearms. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge a handgun, rifle, shotgun or any other type of firearm onto or across the property of another without the express written permission of the owner or other person in legal possession of such property. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge a handgun, rifle, shotgun or any other type of firearm, within an area of the unincorporated portions of the county which is within 250 feet of a residence, place of worship, business or public meeting place. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge a handgun, rifle, shotgun or any other type of firearm in any residential subdivision where lots are five acres or less in area. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful to discharge a handgun, rifle, shotgun or any other type of firearm within 150 feet of any public or private street in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 16-11-103. 
(e)  It shall be unlawful for any person to intentionally, negligently or carelessly discharge a handgun, rifle, shotgun or any other type of firearm in such a manner as to be likely to cause bodily injury or death to persons or cause destruction of property. 
(f)  It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge a handgun, rifle, shotgun or any other type of firearm on any public boat ramp or public dock, or on any public land not designated for such activity. 
(g)  It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge a handgun, rifle, shotgun or any other type of firearm on Sunday, except in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 16-11-105. 
(h)  Special activity permits may be granted as an exception to the provisions of this section by the sheriff's office. Applications for such permits must be submitted to the sheriff's office on the approved form provided by the sheriff's office. Such special activity permits are only available for the day(s) of the event. 
(i)  This section shall not apply when a handgun, rifle, shotgun or any other type of firearm is discharged by any person in defense of self or others in accordance O.C.G.A. § 16-3-21 or in defense of habitation in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 16-3-23. 
(j)  This section shall not apply to any law enforcement officer while in the discharge of his official duties. 
(k)  This section shall not apply to the operation of approved hunting preserves or other shooting ranges. 
(l)  Nothing in this ordinance exempts any person from any state or federal laws relating to firearms. 
(Ord. of 12-4-2007(2), § 1) 
Secs. 50-11—50-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ALARM SYSTEMS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), adopted May 19, 2015, set out provisions intended for use as §§ 50-11.1—50-11.8. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as §§ 50-21—50-28. 

Sec. 50-21. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this article is to encourage alarm users and alarm companies to properly use and maintain alarm systems and to reduce or eliminate false alarms, which unduly divert emergency services from responding to actual emergencies. 
(Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), 5-19-2015) 
Sec. 50-22. - Applicability. 
This article governs fire, medical and security alarm systems intended to summon emergency response from emergency medical, fire department or law enforcement and provides for civil penalties for malfunctions and violations. 
(Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), 5-19-2015) 
Sec. 50-23. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Alarm company means any entity that sells, leases, maintains, services, repairs, alters, replaces, moves, installs or monitors alarm systems in Morgan County. 
Alarm system means any system, device or mechanism intended to detect and signal the occurrence of activity requiring the immediate need for emergency services at the premises at which such device or set of devices is installed. 
Alarm user means any individual or entity, who owns or leases an alarm system or on whose premises an alarm system exists. 
Cancellation means the process whereby an alarm company terminates the need for an emergency response by notifying the emergency communications center after an alarm dispatch request. 
Duress alarm means a silent alarm system signal generated by the manual activation of a device intended to signal a life-threatening situation or crime in progress requiring law enforcement response. 
Emergency response means sheriff's department, fire rescue or emergency medical services response. 
False alarm means the activation of an alarm system to summon emergency personnel which occurs as a result of mechanical or electronic failure, malfunction, improper installation, or the negligence of the alarm user, his/her employees or agents, unless the request for response was cancelled by the alarm user or his/her agent before the sheriff's department, fire rescue or emergency medical services arrives at the alarm site. An alarm is false within the meaning of this article when, sheriff's department, fire rescue, or emergency medical services personnel find no evidence indicating a need for an emergency response, such as: unauthorized entry, robbery, other such crime was committed, attempted, or occurred in or on the premises, which would have activated a properly functioning alarm system; or a fire having occurred which would have activated a properly functioning alarm system; or a medical emergency. Notwithstanding the foregoing, a false alarm shall not include an alarm, which can reasonably be determined to have been caused or activated by violent conditions of nature, nor does it include other extraordinary circumstances not reasonably subject to control by the alarm user or alarm system. In addition, an alarm activated during an alarm system testing procedure shall not be considered a false alarm if the alarm user first notifies and receives permission from the user's alarm company, or designee, to test the system and the alarm company upon receiving such permission does not request emergency dispatch. 
Local alarm means an alarm system that emits a signal at an alarm site that is audible or visible from the exterior of a structure and is not monitored by a remote monitoring facility, whether installed by an alarm company or user. 
Verify means an attempt by the monitoring company, or its representative, to contact the alarm site and/or alarm user by telephone and/or other electronic means, whether or not actual contact with a person is made, to attempt to determine whether an alarm signal is valid before requesting the sheriff's department, fire rescue or emergency medical services for dispatch, in an attempt to avoid an unnecessary alarm dispatch request. For the purpose of this section, telephone verification shall require, as a minimum that a second call be made to a different number if the first attempt fails to reach an alarm user who can properly identify themselves to attempt to determine whether an alarm signal is valid before requesting emergency dispatch. 
(Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), 5-19-2015) 
Sec. 50-24. - Responsibilities of an alarm user. 
An alarm user shall: 
(1)  Maintain the premises and the alarm system in a method that will reduce or eliminate false alarms; 
(2)  Respond or cause a representative to respond to the alarm system's location within 30 minutes upon notification of the need to deactivate a malfunctioning alarm system; to provide right of entry to the premises, or to provide alternative security for the premises; and 
(3)  Ensure that an alarm is not manually activated by the alarm user or any other person for any reason other than an occurrence of an event that the alarm system was intended to report. 
(Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), 5-19-2015) 
Sec. 50-25. - Responsibilities of an alarm company. 
(a)  All alarm companies shall: 
(1)  Obtain and maintain required state and local license(s) and/or permits; 
(2)  Maintain current contact information, which shall be provided to the emergency communications center at the time of a request for emergency response; and 
(3)  Prior to activation of an alarm system, provide verbal and written instructions explaining the proper operation of the alarm system to the alarm user and provide written information on how to obtain service from the alarm company. 
(b)  All alarm companies performing monitoring services shall: 
(1)  Attempt to verify, by calling the alarm site and/or alarm user by telephone, to determine whether an alarm signal is valid before requesting emergency dispatch. Telephone verification shall require, at a minimum, that a second call be made to a different number, if the first attempt fails to reach an alarm user who can properly identify him/herself to attempt to determine whether an alarm signal is valid, except in the case of a panic or robbery-in-progress alarm, or in cases where a crime or fire-in-progress has been verified by video and/or audible means; and maintain required state and local license(s) and/or permits; 
(2)  Communicate a cancellation to the emergency communications center as soon as possible following a determination that response is unnecessary; and 
(3)  Communicate any available information about the location of the alarm. 
(Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), 5-19-2015) 
Sec. 50-26. - Prohibited acts. 
It shall be a violation of this article for an alarm user to: 
(1)  Activate an alarm system for the purpose of summoning an emergency response when no such response is needed because there has been no crime (attempted or committed), no fire, or no medical emergency; 
(2)  Install, maintain, or use an audible alarm system which can sound continually for more than ten minutes; 
(3)  Install, maintain, or use an automatic dial protection device that reports, or causes to be reported, any recorded message to the emergency communications center; or 
(4)  Allow the occurrence of excessive false alarms. 
(Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), 5-19-2015) 
Sec. 50-27. - Enforcement. 
Any violation of any of the provisions of this article shall be civil in nature, shall not constitute a criminal infraction, and shall be punished solely under the provisions of this article. 
(1)  Civil penalties for excessive false alarms . It is hereby found and determined that two or more false alarms during a calendar year is excessive, constitutes a public nuisance, and shall be a violation of this article. Civil penalties for false alarms within any calendar year shall be assessed against an alarm user as follows: 
a.  For the first false alarm in a calendar year, a notice shall be issued to the alarm user, indicating the need to prevent any further false alarms; 
b.  For the second false alarm in a calendar year, a warning shall be issued to the alarm user; 
c.  For the third false alarm in a calendar year, the alarm user shall be charged a $100.00 civil penalty; 
d.  For the fourth false alarm in a calendar year, the alarm user shall be charged a $200.00 civil penalty. 
e.  For the fifth false alarm in a calendar year, the alarm user shall be charged a $300.00 civil penalty. 
f.  For the sixth and all successive false alarms in a calendar year, the alarm user shall be charged a $500.00 civil penalty. 
(2)  Payment . Civil penalties under this article shall be paid within 30 days from the date contained on the notice to the alarm user of the penalty, regardless of the date of actual receipt by the alarm user. 
(3)  Late fee. The failure of an alarm user to make payment of any civil penalties assessed under this article within 30 days from the date contained on the notice shall result in the imposition of a 50 percent late fee, except that the combined penalty and late fee for any single violation shall not exceed $1,000.00. 
(4)  Failure to pay. Following the imposition of any late fees pursuant to this section, Morgan County reserves the right to forward any alarm user's outstanding penalties and late fees to a collection agency should an alarm user fail to make payment within 90 days from the date of the notice of the late fee. Collection fees may be added by the collection agency to the balance owed to the extent allowed by law. In addition, execution may be issued by the county against the property that is the location of the false alarms in the amount of any civil penalties and fines, and such execution shall be recorded upon the general execution docket in the office of the Clerk of the Superior Court of Morgan County, Georgia, and such execution shall constitute a lien on the property, until the same shall have been fully paid and satisfied. Such executions may be enforced in the same manner and with the addition of interest and costs as provided by law for the enforcement of executions for ad valorem taxes for the county. 
(Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), 5-19-2015) 
Sec. 50-28. - Appeals. 
(a)  Board of commissioners to hear appeals. The board of commissioners shall have the power, as further defined in this article, to hear all appeals of decisions and interpretations of the official as outlined in this article. 
(b)  Appeals . 
(1)  Assessment of civil penalties imposed as a result of a violation of this article may be appealed by delivering a written notice of appeal within 14 days of the date contained on the notification of the assessment of such civil penalties. 
(2)  Such written notice of appeal must be actually received by the Director of Planning and Development of Morgan County within this time period, and the failure to deliver such notice within this time period shall constitute an irrevocable waiver of the right to contest the assessment of penalties or other enforcement decisions. 
(3)  Any such written notice of appeal should indicate whether the alarm user desires a hearing. If the alarm user desires a hearing and so indicates in his/her notice of appeal, the alarm user shall be afforded an opportunity for an evidentiary hearing under judicial forms of procedure. Within ten business days of receipt of a notice of appeal requesting a hearing, the county shall notify the alarm user in writing of the date, time and location of the hearing. 
(4)  If the alarm user does not request a hearing, the county shall notify the alarm user of the decision of the board of commissioners in writing within ten business days of the date the decision is rendered. 
(c)  Appeal hearings. For any notice of appeal requesting a hearing, filed in accordance with this article, a record shall be kept, which shall include: 
(1)  The notice of assessment of civil penalty; 
(2)  A record of the oral testimony plus all other evidence received or considered except that oral proceedings or any part thereof shall be transcribed only upon request; and 
(3)  The written decision of the board of commissioners, to be mailed to the alarm user within ten business days of the hearing. 
(d)  Appeals to superior court. An aggrieved alarm user may appeal the decision of the board of commissioners under this article regarding civil penalties for excessive false alarms by appealing to the Superior Court of Morgan County if said appeal is filed within 30 days of the rendering of the decision by the Morgan County Board of Commissioners, and served upon the board pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 9-11-4 within five days of filing. A decision is deemed "rendered" by the board on the date that the board renders its decision, as indicated by the date contained on the decision, not on the date that the minutes reflecting such decision are approved by the board. An appeal from a decision of the board of commissioners under this article is the exclusive remedy for anyone aggrieved by a decision of the board. 
(Ord. No. 2015-001, § 1(exh. A), 5-19-2015) 
Chapter 58 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Garbage and solid waste collection and disposal are authorized as a home rule power of the counties, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(2); Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq.; Litter Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-40 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 58-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Hazardous materials or hazardous waste means waste, in any amount, which is defined, characterized or designated as hazardous by the United States Environmental Protection Agency or appropriate state agency by or pursuant to federal or state law. The term "hazardous waste" shall include motor oil, gasoline, paint, paint cans and items containing Freon, chlorofluorocarbons or other form that may pose an unreasonable risk to health, safety, property and the environment. 
Household garbage means all refuse or trash which is of a size no larger than one foot wide by two feet long and is refuse or trash of a type that is not an appliance or furniture. 
Junked motor vehicle means any motor vehicle, as defined in this section, which does not have lawfully affixed thereto an unexpired license plate or plates, and the condition of which is wrecked, dismantled, partially dismantled, inoperative, abandoned or discarded. 
Litter means all discarded sand, gravel, slag, brickbats, rubbish, waste material, tin cans, refuse, garbage, trash, debris, dead animals or other discarded material of every kind and description which are not waste as such term is defined in this section. 
Motor vehicle means any vehicle which is self-propelled and designed to travel along the ground and shall include, but not be limited to, automobiles, buses, motorbikes, motorcycles, ATVs, trucks, tractors, go-carts, campers and trailers. 
Person means any entity, person, firm, partnership, corporation or unincorporated association. 
Private property means any real property within the county limits, which is privately owned and which is not public property as defined in this section. 
Public property means the right-of-way of any street or highway, which shall include the entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly maintained for the purposes of travel; any body of water or watercourse or the shores or beaches thereof; any publicly owned park, playground, building, refuge, conservation or recreation area. 
Road or street shall be mutually inclusive and shall likewise be deemed to include any alley, lane, court, and other thoroughfare, however described or designated. 
Scrap tires means all tires that are no longer suitable for their original intended purposes because of wear, damage or defect. 
Tire means a hoop of iron, rubber or plastic which is generally designed for encircling the wheel of a motor vehicle and which is neither attached to the motor vehicle nor a part of the motor vehicle as original equipment. 
Waste means all discarded substances and materials whatsoever exceeding ten pounds in weight or 15 cubic feet in volume, or any such substance in any weight or volume, biomedical waste, hazardous waste as defined in this section, a hazardous substance as defined by O.C.G.A. § 12-8-92, or any such substance or material dumped for commercial purposes. The term "waste" includes, without limitation: bottles; boxes; containers; papers; tobacco products; tires; appliances; mechanical equipment or parts; building or construction material; tools; machinery; wood; motor vehicles and motor vehicle parts; vessels; aircraft equipment; waste oil; batteries; antifreeze; sludge from wastewater treatment facility, water supply treatment plant, or air pollution control facility; and air contaminants from any source from any source or facility, and any other discarded material or substance of every kind and description resulting from domestic, industrial, commercial, mining, or governmental operations, including household, commercial, construction and demolition waste, or industrial solid waste which is nonhazardous, nonmedical, and in a form classified as solid waste by the state department of natural resources. 
Yard trimmings means leaves, brush, grass clippings, shrub and tree prunings, discarded Christmas trees, nursery and greenhouse vegetative residuals, and vegetative matter resulting from landscaping development and maintenance other than mining, agricultural, and silvicultural operations. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(1); Ord. of 9-10-2002, § 34-101) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. §§ 12-8-22, 16-7-42. 
Sec. 58-2. - Evidence of violations. 
(a)  Whenever litter is thrown, deposited, dropped, or dumped from any motor vehicle, boat, airplane, or other conveyance in violation of this chapter, it shall be prima facie evidence that the operator of the conveyance has violated this chapter. 
(b)  Whenever any litter which is dumped, deposited, thrown, or left on public or private property in violation of this chapter is discovered to contain any article or articles, including but not limited to letters, bills, publications, or other writings which display the name of a person thereon in such a manner as to indicate that the article belongs or belonged to such person, it shall be a rebuttable presumption that such person has violated this chapter. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(8)) 
Secs. 58-3—58-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DISPOSAL AND TRANSPORTING 

Sec. 58-23. - Waste disposal site. 
(a)  Residents of the county may dispose of household garbage at one of the numerous waste disposal sites located throughout the county for the purpose of collecting such. 
(b)  All items of refuse or trash other than household garbage must be taken to the county transfer station during the hours it is open to the public. 
(c)  No item of garbage of any kind may be placed on top of, adjacent to, or near said waste disposal sites. All items of household garbage must be placed wholly inside said waste disposal sites. 
(d)  Only residents of the county are permitted to make use of waste disposal sites, or dump or place garbage or debris of any kind within the county. 
(e)  Any person charged with violating this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished according to the penalties described in section 1-9. 
(Code 2000, § 12-102) 
Sec. 58-24. - Entry prohibited. 
(a)  Unless so employed or authorized by the county manager, no person shall place any part of his or her person or use any tool to remove or attempt to remove any object or item from any waste disposal site in the county. 
(b)  Any person charged with violating this section shall be charged a fine of at least $25.00 if convicted. 
(Code 2000, § 12-103) 
Sec. 58-25. - Garbage storage areas to be kept clean. 
(a)  The proprietary owner, tenant, or occupant of any premises, and the proprietor and person in charge of every business, commercial, institutional, and industrial establishment, shall be responsible for the sanitary handling and disposition of garbage, litter, waste, scrap tires and refuse on the premises used, occupied or under the control of such person and shall be required to keep the driveways, yards, parking areas, loading or unloading areas and lots adjacent thereto or under the control thereof reasonably clean at all times. 
(b)  Every proprietary owner, occupant, and lessee of a house, business, or building shall be jointly and severally required to maintain garbage storage areas in a clean condition and to ensure that all garbage is properly containerized. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(2)(a); Ord. of 9-10-2002, §§ 34-106, 34-108) 
Sec. 58-26. - Containers required. 
Every proprietary owner, occupant, tenant and person using or occupying any commercial, institutional or industrial building or property in the county shall be obligated, jointly and severally, to provide litter containers of such size, number, and type as may be specified by the county manager or his or her designee to be reasonably required to hold litter generated by operations on the premises. Specifically, and without limiting the generality of the foregoing, the requirement for such containers shall apply to shopping centers, supermarkets, convenience stores, fast food and other type restaurants, service stations and similar establishments and shall likewise apply to commercial establishments, garages, schools, and churches. 
(Code 2000, § 12-101(2)(b); Ord. of 9-10-2002, § 34-107) 
Sec. 58-27. - Construction sites.
